Equality of Rights Upon Acceptance of Jizya
Ruling that acceptance of jizya confers equal inviolability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that upon acceptance of jizya, the life and property of non-Muslims become inviolable like those of Muslims, and explain the proof from the saying of Ali (ra) and its corroboration.

Core Idea
Acceptance of jizya, not actual payment, renders the disbeliever's life and property inviolable.

In this passage, the commentator of Al-Hidayah explains the key moment at which a non-Muslim's life and property become protected under Islamic law. The text clarifies that the critical factor is the acceptance of jizya, not its physical delivery. The proof is drawn from the saying of Ali (ra) and supported by authentic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The subject is disbelievers who accept the call to pay jizya. The ruling: their blood and property become equal to those of Muslims (inviolable).
2
Locate the primary proof
The primary proof is the saying of Ali (ra) transmitted by Imam Shafi'i and Darqutni: 'Their blood is like our blood, their property like our property.'
This is a qawl sahabi.
3
Examine the chain and strength
The narrator chain is weak (da'if), but the meaning is confirmed by authentic hadith in Bukhari and Muslim from Abu Hurairah.
The corroboration strengthens the proof.
4
Clarify key terms
The word 'badhl' in Quduri and 'i'ta' in the Quran (until they give jizya) both mean 'acceptance' of jizya, not physical giving.
This resolves the ambiguity about timing of protection.
5
State the Hanafi position
Upon acceptance of jizya, it becomes wajib (obligatory) for the Islamic state to protect their life and property equally with Muslims.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمْوَالُهُمْ كَأَمْوَالِنَا وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْبَذْلِ الْقُبُولِ وَكَذَا الْمَرَادُ بِالْإِعْطَاءِ الْمَذْكُورِ فِيهِ فِى الْقُرْآنِ وَاللهُ أَعْلَمُ ترجمہ اب اگر ان کافروں نے مسلمانوں کی دعوت قبول کر لی یعنی انہوں نے جزیہ دینا قبول کر لیا تو ان کے لئے انصاف سے وہی کچھ ہو گا جو مسلمانوں کے لئے ہوگا۔ اور انصاف سے ان پر بھی وہی بار ہو گا جو مسلمانوں پر ہوتا ہے۔ حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کے اس فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ کافروں نے اسی لئے جزیہ دینا قبول کیا ہے کہ ان کا خون بھی ہمارے خون کی طرح اور ان کے مال بھی ہمارے مالوں کی طرح محفوظ رہیں ۔ اس کی روایت امام شافعی اور دار قطنی نے کی ہے۔ اگر چہ اس کی اسناد ضعیف ہے۔ پھر بھی صحیحین کی حدیث سے بھی جوابو ہریرہ وغیرہ رضی اللہ عنہ سے مروی ہے یہی معنی ثابت ہوتے ہیں)۔ اور قدوری کے قول میں لفظ بذلوا سے مراد قبول کرنا ہے۔ اور فرمان خداوندی حتی يعطو الجزیہ میں اعطاء سے بھی یہی مراد ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
Their property is like our property, and intended by 'giving' is acceptance, and similarly intended by 'giving' mentioned in the Quran. And Allah knows best. Translation: Now if those disbelievers accepted the call of Muslims, i.e. they accepted to pay jizya, then for them by justice there will be the same as for Muslims, and by justice upon them there will be the same as upon Muslims. Due to the saying of Ali (May Allah be pleased with him) that disbelievers accepted jizya so that their blood be like our blood and their property like our property. This is narrated by Imam Shafi'i and Darqutni, though its chain is weak, yet the same meaning is proven by the hadith of Bukhari and Muslim from Abu Hurairah etc. And in Quduri's saying, the word 'yabdhulu' means acceptance, and in the divine command 'hatta yu'tu al-jizyah' the same is meant. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof. The author explains that when disbelievers accept the call to Islam and agree to pay jizya, their lives and property become inviolable on equal footing with Muslims. The proof is the saying of Ali (ra) reported by Imam Shafi'i and Darqutni, though the chain is weak. However, the same meaning is supported by authentic hadith in Bukhari and Muslim from Abu Hurairah. The author clarifies that the term 'badhl' in Quduri and 'i'ta' in the Quran both mean 'acceptance' of jizya, not merely giving.

Key Terms
الجِزْيَة (al-jizyah): Tax paid by non-Muslims in an Islamic state in lieu of military service.
البَذْل (al-badhl): To give willingly; here used in the sense of acceptance of jizya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when do disbelievers' lives and property become equal to Muslims'?
A) When they actually pay jizya
B) When they accept the call to pay jizya
C) When they convert to Islam
D) When they enter a peace treaty

Key Takeaway
Upon acceptance of jizya, the protection of life and property becomes wajib on the Islamic state, equal to that of Muslims.

Fighting Prohibited Before the Call to Islam
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the call to Islam (da'wah) is wajib before fighting and explain the consequence of omission (sin without financial liability) using the Prophet's hadith as proof.

Core Idea
Fighting without the call is haram; the command 'fad'uhum' makes da'wah wajib.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a foundational rule of Islamic warfare: the call to Islam (da'wah) must precede any military engagement. The author cites the Prophet's explicit instruction to army commanders and explains both the legal obligation and the wisdom behind it. We will unpack the ruling, its proof, and the consequences of violating this command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The text states it is not permissible to fight those who have not received the call. Identify the act being ruled upon: fighting without da'wah.
The ruling is a prohibition (haram) when da'wah is absent.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites the Prophet's hadith: 'Call them to the testimony that there is no god but Allah.' Identify the source and type of dalil.
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator) but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub). Explain how the phrase 'fad'uhum' proves that the call is wajib.
This step connects the linguistic form to the legal ruling.
4
Analyse the Consequence
If fought without call, the Muslims sin but no blood money is due. Understand why the enemy lacks 'ismah (protected status) and the analogy to killing women and insane persons.
Sin arises from violating the command; no diya because no 'ismah.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
The Shafi'i school considers the call sunnah, not wajib. Understand their interpretation and the practical difference.
This step is covered in the madhhab dispute block.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَن يُقَاتَلَ مَنْ لَّمْ تَبْلُغَهُ الدَّعْوَةُ إِلَى الْإِسْلَامِ إِلَّا انْ تَدْعُوهُ لِقَولِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي وَصِيَّةٍ أُمَرَاءِ الْأَجَنَادِ فَادْعُهُمْ إِلى شَهَادَةِ أَن لَّا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَلانَّهُمُ بالدَّعْوَةِ يَعْلَمُونَ أَنَا نُقَاتِلُهُمْ عَلَى الدِّينِ لَا عَلَى سَلْبِ الْأَمْوَالِ وَسَبِّي الدَّرَارِى فَلَعَلَّهُمْ يُحِبُونَ فَتَكَفَى مُؤْنَةَ الْقِتَالِ وَلَوْفَاتَلَهُمُ قَبْلَ الدَّعْوَةِ ايْمَ لِلشَّهِي وَلَا غَرَامَة لِعَدْمِ الْعَاصِمِ وَ أَو الحَرَازُ بِالدَارِ فَصَارَ كَقَتْلِ النِّسْوَانِ وَالمَيِّمَانِ - ترجمہ اور یہ بات جائز نہیں ہے کہ ایسے لوگوں سے قتال کیا جائے جن کو اسلام کی دعوت نہ پہنچی ہو ۔ مگر یہ کہ ان کافروں کو پہلے وہ لوگ دعوت دیدیں ۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اس فرمان کی وجہ سے جو امراء کے لشکر کو وصیت کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ اپنی جگہ پر پہنچ کر پہلے ان لوگوں کو لا الہ الا اللہ کی گواہی کی طرف بلاؤ۔ اور اس وجہ سے کہ اس دعوت دینے سے وہ یقین کر لینگے کہ دوسری صورت میں ہم ان سے دین کے لئے قبال کریں گے۔ اور ان کے مال چھین لینے اور ان کے اہل و عیال کو قید کرنے کے لئے ہم ان سے نہیں لڑیں گے۔ اس طرح اس بات کی امید ہوتی ہے کہ شاید وہ اس دعوت کو آسانی سے قبول کر لیں ۔ پھر ہم بھی ان سے لڑائی کی پریشانیوں سے بچ جائیں گے۔ (اور وہ بھی بچ جائیں گے اور اگر مسلمانوں نے ان کو دعوت دینے سے پہلے ہی ان سے قتال کر لیا تو یہ مسلمان ممانعت کی خلاف ورزی کرنے کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوں گے۔ لیکن ان کے خونوں کے ضامن بھی نہ ہوں گے کیونکہ کوئی چیز موجب عصمت بھی نہیں ہے۔ یعنی دین اسلام یا دار الاسلام کی حفاظت نہیں ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے حملہ کرنے میں کافروں کی عورتیں یا بچے قتل ہو جائیں۔
It is not permissible to fight those who have not received the call to Islam unless you call them first. Due to his (peace be upon him) saying in the will to the commanders of armies: Call them to the testimony that there is no god but Allah. And because by the call they will know that we fight them for religion, not to seize wealth and capture offspring, so perhaps they will accept and the burden of fighting will be removed. And if they fought them before the call, they sin [؟] and no compensation due to lack of protected status. Or the fortress by the home, so it becomes like killing women and insane persons. Translation: ... [as in Urdu]
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that it is forbidden to fight any group until the call to Islam has reached them, based on the Prophet's instruction to commanders to invite enemies to the shahadah before engaging. This call informs them that the motive is religious, not plunder, and may lead to peaceful acceptance. If Muslims attack without calling, they commit a sin (because they violated the command) but no financial compensation (diya or kaffarah) is required because the enemy had no protected status (isam). The author analogizes this to accidentally killing women and children in a raid, where sin exists but no monetary liability.

Key Terms
الدَّعْوَة (al-da'wah): The call to Islam before initiating war.
العِصْمَة (al-'ismah): Inviolability of life and property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Muslims fight a group that has not received the call to Islam, what are the consequences per the text?
A) They are sinful and must pay blood money
B) They are sinful but no blood money is due
C) They are not sinful if the enemy is hostile
D) They must compensate the enemy

Key Takeaway
The call to Islam is wajib before combat; fighting without it is haram and sinful, but no compensation is due because the enemy lacks protected status.

Re-calling to Islam is Mustahabb, Not Wajib
Ruling that re-calling already called enemies is recommended, not obligatory, with prophetic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on re-calling enemies to Islam before attack and explain why it is mustahabb not wajib, citing the prophetic dalil.

Core Idea
Re-calling already-called enemies is recommended, not required, as proven by the Prophet's surprise raids.

This lesson addresses a specific question in the siyar (military law) of the Hanafi school: when a Muslim army faces enemies who have already received the call to Islam, must they call again before attacking? The text clarifies that a second call is mustahabb, not wajib, and provides prophetic precedent. It also discusses when the recommendation may be abandoned due to harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
Recognise that the act being discussed is calling enemies to Islam a second time before attack. Determine whether it is obligatory, recommended, or something else.
The text explicitly says it is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the evidence cited: the Prophet's (peace be upon him) surprise attack on Banu Mustaliq while they were heedless, and his instruction to Usama to raid at dawn and burn.
These are from authentic hadith collections (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Analyse how the proof shows non-obligation: the Prophet himself did not call again before these attacks. If it were obligatory, he would not have omitted it.
The absence of a second call in these actions indicates that it is not required.
4
Note the exceptions and conditions
The commentary adds that if there is a strong fear that a re-call will give the enemy time to prepare and harm Muslims, the recommendation may be abandoned. This balances the recommendation with the principle of avoiding harm.
The default is mustahabb, but maslahah can override it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوبارہ دعوت اسلام کا حکم وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يَدْعُوا مَنْ بَلَعَتْهُ الدَّعْوَةُ مُبَالَعَةً فِي الْإِندَارِ وَ لَا يَجِبُ ذَالِكَ لأَنه صَحَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَغَارَ عَلَى بَنِي الْمُصْطَلِقِ وَهُمْ غَارُونَ وَ عَهِدَ إِلى أَسَامَةَ أَنْ يُغِيْرَ عَلَى ابْنِى صَبَاحًا ثُمَّ يُحْرِقُ وَالْعَارَةُ لَا يَكُونُ بِدَعْوَةٍ ترجمہ اور جن کفار کو اسلام کی دعوت پہنچ چکی ہے ان کو بھی قتال کرنے سے پہلے دوبارہ دعوت دینا مستحب ہے تا کہ زیادہ سے زیادہ اندار کا کام ہو جائے ۔ مگر ایسا کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بنو مصطلق (قبیلہ خزاعہ کی ایک شاخ ) پر اس طرح چھاپہ مارا کہ وہ غافل تھے۔ (رواہ البخاری و مسلم) اسی طرح حضرت اسامہ بن زید پر لازم کر دیا تھا کہ فلسطین میں ایک جگہ اپنی میں صبح کے وقت چھاپا مار میں پھر اس جگہ کو جلا دیں ۔ رواہ ابوداؤ دو ابن ماجہ ۔ اور چھاپا مارنے سے پہلے دعوت نہیں دی جاتی ہے۔ تشريح وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَن يَدْعُو الخ ایک بار دشمنوں کو دعوت دے کر ان پر حملہ کرنے سے پہلے بھی دوبارہ دعوت دینی مستحب ہے۔ اس زمانہ میں اگر چہ اسلام مشرق و مغرب میں خوب پھیل چکا ہے۔ پھر بھی بعض علاقے ایسے ہیں جن کو اسلام کا کچھ بھی شعور نہیں ہے۔ پھر اگر چہ ان کو نفس اسلام کی خبر مل چکی ہے مگر ان کو جزیہ دینے سے متعلق کوئی علم نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اب بھی جزیہ کی دعوت دیئے بغیر ان سے قتال نہیں کرنا چاہئے۔ البتہ اگر غالب گمان یہ ہو کہ اگر ان کو بطور استجاب دعوت اسلام دی جائے گی تو اس سے مسلمانوں کو خطرہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ وہ فوڑا اپنا سامان مہیا کر لیں گے۔ یا اپنے قلعہ کو درست کر لیں گے۔ تو دوبارہ دعوت کو ترک کر دینا چاہیئے۔
The ruling of re-calling to Islam: It is recommended that they call those who have already received the call, as an emphasis in warning, and it is not obligatory, because it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) raided Banu Mustaliq while they were heedless, and he charged Usama to raid [someone] at dawn then burn, and raiding is not preceded by a call. Translation: ... [as in Urdu]
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the case where enemies have already received the call to Islam. The Hanafi ruling is that it is mustahabb (recommended) to call them again before attacking, to maximize the warning, but it is not wajib. The proof is the Prophet's surprise attack on Banu Mustaliq and his instruction to Usama to raid at dawn and burn, both without a prior call. The commentary adds a practical nuance: if there is a strong fear that a re-call will give the enemy time to prepare, it may be abandoned. This shows the principle of maslahah overriding the recommendation.

Key Terms
الغَارَة (al-gharah): A surprise military raid without prior notice.
مُسْتَحَبّ (mustahabb): Recommended but not obligatory; omission is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary proof that re-calling enemies to Islam before attack is not wajib?
A) The Prophet's statement that it is not required.
B) The Prophet's practice of surprise attacks without a second call.
C) The consensus of the Companions.
D) The principle of necessity overriding obligations.

Key Takeaway
Re-calling enemies who have already received the call to Islam is mustahabb, not wajib, as demonstrated by the Prophet's own practice of surprise raids.

The Three-Step Sequence Before Battle
Ruling with proof: step-by-step war justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three-step sequence before fighting in Hanafi law and derive the ruling from the hadith of Sulayman ibn Burayda.

Core Idea
Fighting is the last resort: only after rejecting Islam and jizya.

This passage from Al-Hidayah concludes the three-step approach to non-Muslim enemies. Understanding this sequence is essential for knowing when war becomes obligatory in the Hanafi school. The proof is a clear hadith, reinforced by the principle that Allah alone grants victory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled? Fighting after the enemy has refused both the call to Islam and the offer of jizya. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) as fard kifayah.
The obligation is collective, not individual.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Sulayman ibn Burayda, which commands: 'If they refuse, seek help from Allah and fight them.'
The hadith is narrated by Muslim and the Sunan.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form (فَاسْتَعِنْ, قَاتِلُهُمْ) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. The command is clear and unqualified.
Dalala is qat'i despite zanni thubut.
4
Identify the sequence
The hadith establishes a clear order: first call to Islam, then offer jizya, then fight. Fighting is only the third step.
This prevents hasty warfare.
5
Assess the authority
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) muttafaq alayh. It is relied upon in Zahir al-Riwayah.
The ruling is mufta bihi and cross-madhhab agreed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِنْ أَبُو ذَالِكَ اسْتَعَانُوا بِاللَّهِ عَلَيْهِمْ وَحَارَبُؤُهُمْ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي حَدِيثِ سُلَيْمَانَ بْنِ بَرِيْدَةَ فَإِنْ أَبَوَاذَالِكَ فَادْعُهُمْ إِلَى إِعْطَاءِ الْجِزْيَةِ إِلى أَنْ قَالَ فَإِنْ أَبَوْهَا فَاسْتَعِنْ بِاللَّهِ عَلَيْهِمْ وَقَاتِلُهُمْ وَلأَنَّهُ تَعَالَى هُوَ النَّاصِرُ لاَوْلِيَائِهِ وَالْمُدمر على أَعْدَائِهِ فَيُسْتَعَانُ بِهِ فِي كُلِ الْأُمُورِ ترجمہ کہا دعوت اسلام کے بعد بھی اگر کفار جزیہ دینے سے بھی انکار کر دیں تو اہل اسلام اللہ عزوجل سے ان کے خلاف مدد کی درخواست کر کے ان سے مقابلہ کریں۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اس فرمان کی وجہ سے جو کہ حضرت سلیمان بن بریدہ رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ اگر دشمن کلمہ شہادت کہنے کی دعوت قبول کرنے سے انکار کر دیں تو ان کو جزیہ دینے کی دعوت دو۔ یہاں تک کہ فرمایا کہ اگر وہ جزیہ دینے سے بھی انکار کر دیں تو ان کے خلاف اللہ سے مدد چاہو پھر ان سے قتال شروع کردو۔ (رواہ مسلم و سنن اربعہ ) اور اس دلیل سے بھی مدد چاہئے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ ہی اپنے خاص بندوں کو فتح دینے والا اور اپنے دشمنوں کو ہلاک کرنے والا ہے ۔ اس لئے تمام معاملات میں اسی سے مدد طلب کرنا چاہئے ۔
He said: If they refuse that, then seek help from Allah against them and fight them, due to his (peace be upon him) saying in the hadith of Sulayman ibn Burayda: If they refuse that, then call them to give jizya, until he said: If they refuse it, then seek help from Allah against them and fight them. And because Allah Almighty is the Helper of His allies and the Destroyer of His enemies, so He is sought for help in all matters. Translation: ... [as in Urdu]
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It concludes the sequence: if enemies reject both the call to Islam and the offer of jizya, Muslims are commanded to seek help from Allah and then wage war. The primary proof is the hadith of Sulayman ibn Burayda, which clearly outlines the three-step process: call to Islam, then jizya, then fight. The commentary adds a secondary rational proof: Allah is the only true helper, so all affairs should begin with seeking His aid. This establishes tawakkul as part of the military strategy.

Key Terms
الِاسْتِعَانَة (al-isti'anah): Seeking help from Allah before battle.
جِزْيَة (jizyah): A tax paid by non-Muslims under Muslim protection, offered before fighting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Call to Islam, then fight immediately
B) Call to Islam, then jizya, then fight
C) Call to jizya, then Islam, then fight
D) Fight first, then call

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, war is only permitted after both the call to Islam and the offer of jizya have been refused.

Permissibility of Using Catapults and Burning Enemy Territory
Ruling on catapults and burning with prophetic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using catapults and burning enemy territory, and identify the prophetic precedent that establishes its permissibility.

Core Idea
The Prophet's own battlefield actions provide direct permission for catapults and burning.

This short passage from al-Hidayah addresses whether the use of siege engines and burning enemy lands is lawful in war. The answer relies not on abstract reasoning but on concrete precedent from the Prophet himself. As you read, note how the Hanafi school anchors permissibility in the Sunnah al-fi'liyyah (the Prophet's actions), which carries binding authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Acts and Their Ruling
The passage mentions two specific military actions: setting up catapults (manjaniq) and burning enemy territory. Determine the legal status (hukm) the text assigns to them.
The text uses a direct command form (yanabu an yaf'alu) or permission? The Urdu commentary clarifies that both are permissible.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The text cites two incidents from the Prophet's military campaigns: the use of a catapult at Ta'if and the burning of al-Buwayrah. Identify these as the proof (dalil).
These are acts (fi'l) of the Prophet, which in Hanafi usul indicate permissibility unless proven otherwise.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the Prophet's actions serve as a proof. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's actions are a source of legislation. Here, the fact that he did something means it is permissible for the ummah, without the need for a command.
This is based on the principle that the actions of the Prophet indicate permissibility (al-fi'l yadullu 'ala al-ibahah).
4
Confirm Absence of Contradictory Evidence
Check if there is any counter-proof that would prohibit these acts. The text implies none; the commentator notes that these methods are allowed as long as war continues.
If there were a prohibition, it would outweigh the permissibility derived from the action.
5
Conclude the Ruling
State the final ruling: both catapults and burning enemy territory are permissible (mubah) in jihad. This is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.
The ruling is based on clear prophetic precedent, making it strong (zahir al-riwayah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ نَصَبُوا عَلَيْهِمُ الْمَجَانِيقَ كَمَا نَصَبَ رَسُولُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَى الطَّائِفِ وَحَرِّفُوهُمْ لأَنه عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ احترق البويرة ترجمہ اوران کفار پر مقابلہ کی غرض سے وہ منجنیق قائم کر دیں۔ جیسا کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے طائف پر منجنیق قائم کر دی تھی ۔ اور ان دشمنوں کے علاقوں کو جلا دیں جیسا کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے موضع بوسیرہ کو جلا دیا تھا۔ تشريح وَنَصَبُو اعْلَيْهِمُ الْمَجَانِيقَ الخ کفار سے مقاتلہ جاری رہنے کی صورت میں ان پر منجنیق کے ذریعہ پتھر سے حملہ کیا جا سکتا ہے اور ان کو آگ سے جلایا بھی جاسکتا ہے جیسا کہ رسول اللہ ا سے بھی بویرہ (باء کوضمہ اور و اوکوفتہ کے ساتھ ایک مقام کا نام ) کو جلا

Commentary: ... [as in Urdu]

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It permits the use of siege engines (catapults) to stone enemy positions and burning their lands, citing the Prophet's actions at Ta'if and Buwayrah. The commentary notes that both methods are allowed when war continues. This establishes that even harsh measures (like burning) are permissible within the bounds set by the Prophet's example.

Key Terms
المَنْجَنِيق (al-manjaneq): A siege weapon that hurls stones.
البُوَيْرَة (al-buwayrah): A place (or palm grove) that the Prophet burned.
فِعْل (fi'l): An action of the Prophet; in Hanafi usul, it serves as a source of law indicating permissibility unless proven otherwise.

Calling the Enemy to Islam Before Attack
Explains the ruling on calling the enemy to Islam and jizyah before fighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on calling the enemy to Islam before combat, identify the evidence (dalil) that establishes it, and apply the exception when the call poses a risk.

Core Idea
Calling the enemy to Islam is wajib before the first attack; a second call is mustahab unless it enables the enemy to prepare for battle.

In the context of jihad, the Hanafi school emphasizes that da'wah (calling to Islam) must precede qital (fighting). This lesson examines the ruling: the initial call is obligatory (wajib), while a second call is recommended (mustahab) but can be omitted if it endangers Muslims. The proof is drawn from the hadith of Sulayman ibn Buraydah and the broader principle that Allah alone grants victory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is calling the enemy to Islam (or jizyah) before initiating combat. Determine the hukm level: the first call is wajib (obligatory), the second call is mustahab (recommended).
The passage explicitly says 'yustahabbu' for the second call, indicating it is not mandatory.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The primary proof is the hadith of Sulayman ibn Buraydah, where the Prophet ﷺ commanded to call the enemy to Islam, then to jizyah, and if they refuse, to seek Allah's help and fight.
This hadith is ahad (singular transmission) thus zanni al-thubut, but its dalalah (meaning) is clear (qati).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (point of inference)
The imperative form 'ادعوهم' (call them) in the hadith indicates obligation (wujub) per Hanafi usul. Similarly, 'قاتلوهم' (fight them) indicates the obligation to fight after the call is rejected.
The Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub (a command indicates obligation).
4
Note the exception and the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The commentator mentions that if a second call would enable the enemy to prepare and cause danger, it may be abandoned. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to prevent harm.
This exception applies only to the second call; the first call is never omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشريح وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَن يَدْعُو الخ ایک بار دشمنوں کو دعوت دے کر ان پر حملہ کرنے سے پہلے بھی دوبارہ دعوت دینی مستحب ہے۔ اس زمانہ میں اگر چہ اسلام مشرق و مغرب میں خوب پھیل چکا ہے۔ پھر بھی بعض علاقے ایسے ہیں جن کو اسلام کا کچھ بھی شعور نہیں ہے۔ پھر اگر چہ ان کو نفس اسلام کی خبر مل چکی ہے مگر ان کو جزیہ دینے سے متعلق کوئی علم نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اب بھی جزیہ کی دعوت دیئے بغیر ان سے قتال نہیں کرنا چاہئے۔ البتہ اگر غالب گمان یہ ہو کہ اگر ان کو بطور استجاب دعوت اسلام دی جائے گی تو اس سے مسلمانوں کو خطرہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ وہ فوڑا اپنا سامان مہیا کر لیں گے۔ یا اپنے قلعہ کو درست کر لیں گے۔ تو دوبارہ دعوت کو ترک کر دینا چاہیئے۔ کفار اسلام قبول کرنے اور جزیہ دینے سے انکار کر دیں تو استعانت باللہ سے حملہ شروع کر دیں قَالَ فَإِنْ أَبَوْا ذَالِكَ اسْتَعَانُوا بِاللَّهِ عَلَيْهِمْ وَحَارَبُؤُهُمْ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي حَدِيثِ سُلَيْمَانَ بْنِ بَرِيْدَةَ فَإِنْ أَبَوَاذَالِكَ فَادْعُهُمْ إِلَى إِعْطَاءِ الْجِزْيَةِ إِلى أَنْ قَالَ فَإِنْ أَبَوْهَا فَاسْتَعِنْ بِاللَّهِ عَلَيْهِمْ وَقَاتِلُهُمْ وَلأَنَّهُ تَعَالَى هُوَ النَّاصِرُ لاَوْلِيَائِهِ وَالْمُدمر على أَعْدَائِهِ فَيُسْتَعَانُ بِهِ فِي كُلِ الْأُمُورِ
Explanation: 'It is recommended that he calls...' Once he has called the enemies and then before attacking, it is recommended to call them a second time. In this time, even though Islam has spread widely in the east and west, still there are some areas that have no knowledge of Islam at all. Then, even if they have heard of Islam itself, they have no knowledge of giving jizyah. Therefore, one should not fight them without calling them to jizyah. However, if it is strongly thought that if they are called to Islam by way of response it may cause danger to Muslims because they will prepare their equipment or repair their fort, then the second call should be abandoned. If the disbelievers refuse to accept Islam and to give jizyah, then seek Allah's help and begin the attack. He (al-Quduri) said: 'Then if they refuse that, seek help from Allah against them and fight them' because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Sulayman ibn Buraydah: 'Then if they refuse that, call them to giving jizyah' until he said: 'Then if they refuse it, seek help from Allah against them and fight them.' And also because Allah Almighty is the Helper of His allies and the Destroyer of His enemies, so help is sought from Him in all matters.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the ruling that it is recommended to call the enemy to Islam before engaging in combat. The commentator explains that the call should be made even if Islam is widespread, as there may still be people unaware of the obligation of jizyah. However, if the call would enable the enemy to prepare for battle, it may be abandoned. The ruling then states that after calling, if the enemy refuses both Islam and jizyah, the Muslims should seek Allah's help and fight. This is supported by the hadith of Sulayman ibn Buraydah and the general principle that Allah alone grants victory.

Key Terms
دعوت (da'wah): The call to Islam or jizyah before initiating combat
جزیة (jizyah): A tax imposed on dhimmis (protected non-Muslims) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on calling the enemy to Islam before fighting?
A) It is recommended but not required.
B) It is obligatory (wajib) at least once.
C) It is only required if the enemy has not heard of Islam.
D) it is not required if the enemy is far from Muslim lands.

Key Takeaway
Calling the enemy to Islam before fighting is a wajib once; a second call is mustahab unless it exposes Muslims to harm.

The Permissibility of Siege Weapons and Burning Enemy Property
States the permissibility of using mangonel and fire against the enemy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using siege weapons and burning enemy property, cite the prophetic precedent, and explain the extension to modern warfare.

Core Idea
The Prophet's actions at Ta'if and Buwayrah establish permission for any effective siege weapon and destruction of enemy resources.

Warfare in the Hanafi school is guided by prophetic practice and the overarching goal of weakening the enemy while avoiding unnecessary cruelty. This passage addresses two common siege tactics—using a mangonel (catapult) and setting fire to enemy property—and grounds their permissibility in explicit prophetic actions. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the Islamic ethics of military engagement and the concept of qiyas (analogical reasoning) to modern weapons.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and identify the core acts
The passage rules that it is permissible to set up mangonels against the enemy and to set fire to their property. Identify these two acts as the subject of the ruling.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) and not obligatory.
2
Locate the prophetic precedent for each act
For the mangonel, the evidence is the Prophet's action at Ta'if. For burning, it is the burning of the date palms of Banu Nadir at Buwayrah. Note the hadith sources (Bukhari and Muslim).
These are acts of the Prophet (fi'l) which indicate permissibility in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the rational extension (qiyas) to modern equivalents
The commentator explicitly states that the mangonel's function (hurling stones) is now performed by cannons, and the same ruling applies. This is qiyas awlawi (a fortiori): if primitive weapons are allowed, more effective ones are also allowed.
The principle of qiyas here is that any means achieving the same end (weakening the enemy) is permissible.
4
Note the limitation: burning property vs. burning persons
The hadith of Buwayrah only proves burning property (trees). The commentator argues that burning persons is also permissible by analogy to killing, based on the aim of removing corruption. However, this is a derived ruling, not directly from the hadith.
Some scholars prohibit burning persons due to the hadith 'only Allah punishes with fire'—a point of ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf on burning
The Hanafi position permits burning if it serves the purpose of weakening the enemy. Some other schools restrict it. Note the practical consequence: Hanafis allow scorched-earth tactics when necessary.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi view relies on the general permissibility of harming the enemy within the laws of war.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ نَصَبُوا عَلَيْهِمُ الْمَجَانِيقَ كَمَا نَصَبَ رَسُولُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَى الطَّائِفِ وَحَرِّفُوهُمْ لأَنه عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ احترق البويرة ترجمہ اوران کفار پر مقابلہ کی غرض سے وہ منجنیق قائم کر دیں۔ جیسا کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے طائف پر منجنیق قائم کر دی تھی ۔ اور ان دشمنوں کے علاقوں کو جلا دیں جیسا کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے موضع بوسیرہ کو جلا دیا تھا۔ تشريح وَنَصَبُو اعْلَيْهِمُ الْمَجَانِيقَ الخ کفار سے مقاتلہ جاری رہنے کی صورت میں ان پر منجنیق کے ذریعہ پتھر سے حملہ کیا جا سکتا ہے اور ان کو آگ سے جلایا بھی جاسکتا ہے جیسا کہ رسول اللہ ا سے بھی بویرہ (باء کوضمہ اور و اوکوفتہ کے ساتھ ایک مقام کا نام ) کو جلا دیا تھا۔ منجنیق میم کو کسرہ کے ساتھ واحد سے جمع مجانیق ۔ مجانیق منجیقات۔ فلاخن .. ایک بڑا گو پھیا جس سے قلعوں پر پتھر مار کر اسے توڑنے کی کوشش کی جاتی تھی ۔ اور وہی کام اب تو پوں سے لیا جاتا ہے جس کی وجہ سے وہ تقریبا متروک ہو گیا ہے۔ لیکن حدیث سے اس بات کی دلیل ہوتی ہے کہ تو پوں سے حملہ کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ اور بویرہ کے جلانے کی حدیث یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے یہود اور نبی نضیر کے کھجوروں کے درخت جلوا دئیے اور کٹوا ڈالے تھے ۔ رواہ البخاری ومسلم اس حدیث سے یہ ثابت نہیں ہوتا ہے کہ خود کفار کو بھی جلانا جائز ہے لیکن ان کے فساد دور کرنے کے لئے قتل کرنے کی طرح ان کا جلانا بھی جائز ہے۔
And they set up mangonels against them as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) set up mangonels against Ta'if, and they set fire to them because he (peace be upon him) burned al-Buwayrah. Translation: And they set up mangonels against the disbelievers for the purpose of confrontation, just as the Prophet (peace be upon him) set up mangonels against Ta'if. And they burn the enemies' areas just as the Prophet (peace be upon him) burned the place of Buwayrah. Explanation: 'And they set up mangonels against them,' etc., in the case of ongoing combat with the disbelievers, one may attack them with stones using the mangonel and may burn them with fire, just as the Prophet (peace be upon him) burned Buwayrah (with damma on ba and vowels, the name of a place). Mangonel: with kasra on mim, singular; plural majaniq, majaniq, majaniqat, falaakhun... a large catapult with which stones are thrown at forts to break them. Today, cannons are used for this work, which is why it has become almost obsolete. But the hadith indicates that attacking with cannons is also permissible. As for the hadith of burning Buwayrah, the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the burning and cutting down of the date palms of the Jews of Banu Nadir. (Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim). This hadith does not prove that it is permissible to burn the disbelievers themselves, but just as killing them is permissible to remove their corruption, burning them is also permissible.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of using certain siege techniques against the enemy during war. The author first states that Muslims may set up mangonels (catapults) against the enemy, citing the Prophet's action at Ta'if. Similarly, they may set fire to enemy property, as the Prophet burned the date palms of Banu Nadir at al-Buwayrah. The commentary elaborates that the mangonel was an ancient siege weapon, and its modern equivalent (cannons) is also permissible. It clarifies that burning property is allowed, but burning living enemies is addressed separately: while the hadith about burning trees does not directly prove burning persons, the commentator argues that since killing is allowed, burning is also permissible as a means to destroy the enemy's power.

Key Terms
منجنیق (manjaniq): A catapult or mangonel used in siege warfare to hurl stones at enemy fortifications

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the permissibility of using a mangonel (manjaniq) against the enemy?
A) The general command to fight.
B) The Prophet's use of it at Ta'if.
C) The necessity to destroy fortresses.
D) The consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the use of any effective siege weapon and destruction of enemy property based on prophetic precedent, with the condition that it serves a legitimate military purpose.

Destroying Enemy Resources in War: Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on destroying enemy resources during war

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on destroying enemy crops and trees during war, identify the condition that makes it makruh, and apply the ruling to a scenario.

Core Idea
Destroying enemy resources is permissible to weaken them, but becomes disliked when victory is certain.

War is a harsh reality, and Islamic law provides guidance even in the heat of battle. This passage from Al-Quduri's matn addresses a specific question: is it permissible to flood enemy lands, cut down their trees, and destroy their crops? The Hanafi school answers with a clear ruling based on the objective of weakening the enemy, but adds a crucial condition that prevents wanton destruction when victory is already assured.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific actions are being discussed? (releasing water, cutting trees, destroying crops). What is the default hukm? (mubah/permissible).
The passage states these actions are 'legislated' (mashru'), meaning permissible.
2
Extract the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
Why are these actions permissible? The author gives a reason: they cause humiliation, anger, breaking of power, and dispersal of the enemy. This is the 'illa (effective cause).
The ta'lil shows that the permissibility is linked to military necessity.
3
Identify the condition that changes the ruling
The commentary adds a condition: if victory is strongly expected, then cutting fruit-bearing trees and spoiling crops becomes makruh (disliked). Why? Because the necessity is no longer present.
This condition prevents unnecessary destruction and aligns with the principle of not exceeding what is needed.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a situation where Muslim forces are on the verge of victory. Should they still destroy enemy crops? According to the Hanafi school, they should avoid it as it is makruh.
The ruling is nuanced and depends on the tactical situation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَأَرْسَلُوا عَلَيْهِمُ المَاءَ وَقَطَعُوا أَشْجَارَهُمْ وَأَفْسَدُوا رُرُوعَهُمْ لِأَنَّ فِي جَمِيعِ ذَالِكَ إِلْحَاقَ الْكَبْتِ وَالْغَيْظِ بِهِمْ وَكَسْرَ شَوْكَتِهِمْ وَتَفْرِيْقَ جَعِهِمْ فَيَكُونُ مَشْرُوعًا ترجمہ اور قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ اور کافروں اور دشمنوں پر پانی کا سیلاب رواں کر دیں یعنی اگر موقع ملے تو ان کو پانی میں ڈبو دیں۔ اور ان کے درخت کاٹ دیں۔ اور ان کی کھیتیاں خراب کر دیں کیونکہ ان تمام کاموں سے کافروں کی ذلت اور ان کی بربادی اور ان کو غم میں ڈالنا اور ان کی طاقت کو کچلنا اور ان کی جماعت کو متفرق اور تتر بتر اور منتشر کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے ان میں کا ہر فعل جائز ہوگا۔ (اور اگر غالب گمان ہو کہ اب اسلام کی فتح ہوگی تو ایسی صورت میں پھل دار درختوں کا نا شنا اور کھیتی کو نقصان پہنچا نا کر وہ ہوگا)۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And they release water against them, and cut down their trees, and spoil their crops, because in all that there is humiliating them, angering them, breaking their power, and dispersing their gathering, so it is legislated. Translation: And al-Quduri said: And they release a flood of water upon the disbelievers and enemies, i.e., if they get an opportunity, drown them in water. And cut down their trees, and spoil their fields, because in all these actions there is humiliation of the disbelievers, their destruction, causing them grief, crushing their power, and scattering and dispersing their group. Therefore, every act among these is permissible. (And if it is strongly thought that the victory of Islam is imminent, then cutting down fruit-bearing trees and harming crops is disliked.)
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn (Al-Quduri) and its commentary stating that during war, Muslims may flood enemy lands, cut down trees, and destroy crops. The reason (ta'lil) is that these actions weaken and humiliate the enemy, thereby serving the purpose of jihad. The commentator adds a caveat: if Muslim victory is already certain, then such destruction may be disliked (makruh) because it is unnecessary. The ruling is based on the general principle of inflicting harm on the enemy to break their power.

Key Terms
اسلحه (asliha): Weapons; in this context, means of war including water, fire, etc.
كبت (kabt): Humiliation, subjugation; one of the purposes of the destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the enemy is likely to surrender.
B) When the trees are outside the battlefield.
C) When Muslim victory is already certain.
D) When the enemy has not attacked first.

Key Takeaway
Destroying enemy resources is permissible when it weakens them, but becomes disliked if victory is already certain—showing that Islamic law balances necessity with avoiding waste.

Shooting at Enemy Fort Containing Muslim Prisoners
Ruling on attacking enemy fort with Muslim captives, with qiyas reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on attacking an enemy fortress with Muslim prisoners and explain the qiyas reasoning based on the principle of repelling general harm.

Core Idea
Repelling general harm from Islam outweighs specific harm to individuals, permitting attack even with Muslim captives inside.

This passage addresses a critical question in jihad: when an enemy fort holds Muslim captives, can we still attack? The Hanafi school answers yes, grounding this in a powerful legal principle. Let's unpack the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? What is the hukm level (mubah, haram, etc.)?
The act is attacking an enemy fortress, and the ruling is mubah (permissible).
2
Locate the dalil (qiyas)
What proof does the author cite? Here it is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) based on the principle of repelling general harm.
The proof is aqli (rational), not a direct text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does the qiyas prove the ruling? Identify the illa (effective cause) and how it links the original case (asl) to the new case (far').
The illa is the general benefit outweighing specific harm.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? What is their proof?
The Shafi'i school prohibits such attacks if Muslims are known to be present.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon as mufta bihi and why?
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi based on the overriding necessity of protecting the Muslim community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمِّيهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمُ أسير أو تاجِرُ لِدَفَعِ الضَّرَرِ الْعَامِ بِالَّذَتِّ عَنْ بَيْضَةِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَقَتْلُ الأَسِيرِ وَالتَّاجِرِ ضَرَرٌ حَاصٌ وَ لأَنَّهُ فَكَمَا يَحْلُو حِصْنَ عَنْ مُسْلِمٍ فَلَوِ امْتَعَ بِاعْتِبَارِهِ لَا نُسَدَّ بَابَةً وا ترجمہ اور کا فردشمنوں پر پتھر برسانے میں بھی کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اگر چہ ان میں مسلمان قیدی یا تاجر بھی موجود ہوں۔ کیونکہ ان پر پتھر برسانے میں مسلمانوں کی بڑی جماعت سے عمومی طریقہ سے نقصان دہ چیزوں سے بچانا مقصود ہوتا ہے اور چند یا ایک دو مسلمان یا تاجر کا مر جانا صرف اسی ایک دو فرد کا قتل ہو جانا یہ شخصی نقصان ہوتا ہے۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ ایسی صورت کم ہی ہوتی ہے کہ کوئی قلعہ مسلمان سے بالکل خالی ہوتا ہو۔ اس لئے اگر مسلمان کا خیال کر کے ایسا کرنا منع کر دیا جائے تو جہاد کا دروازہ ہی بند ہو جائے گا۔ (اسی طرح اگر کافروں کے قلعہ میں چند مسلمان خواہ قیدی یا تاجر کسی طرح کے ہوں تو قلعہ کے اندر تو یوں کے گولے گرانا بھی جائز ہوگا ۔ البتہ اس صورت میں صرف کافروں کے قتل کی نیت ہونی چاہئے ۔ اگر چہ ضمنا مسلماں بھی مارے جائیں۔
And there is no harm in shooting at them even if there is a Muslim prisoner or trader among them, to repel general harm from the core of Islam, while the killing of the prisoner and trader is specific harm. And because (for) as a fortress is not devoid of a Muslim, so if one were to abstain due to consideration of him, the door would be closed. Translation: And there is no harm in throwing stones at the enemies even if there are Muslim captives or traders among them. Because in throwing stones at them, the intention is to repel harmful things from the great majority of Muslims in a general way, while the death of one or two Muslims or traders is only the killing of that one or two individuals, which is a personal harm. And also by the proof that such a situation is rare that a fortress is completely empty of Muslims. Therefore, if this action were prohibited out of consideration for a Muslim, the door of jihad would be closed. (Similarly, if there are a few Muslims in the enemy's fort, whether captives or traders, it is permissible to drop cannonballs inside the fort. However, in this case, the intention should be only to kill the disbelievers, even if Muslims are killed incidentally.)
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that it is permissible to attack an enemy fortification even if there are Muslim prisoners or traders inside. The reason is that the benefit to the entire Muslim community (repelling general harm) outweighs the specific harm to those individuals. Additionally, the argument is made that if such attacks were prohibited due to the presence of any Muslim, the door of jihad would effectively be closed, as forts are rarely completely free of Muslims. The commentator adds that when firing, one should intend only to kill the disbelievers, even if Muslims are unintentionally harmed. This is a classic application of the Hanafi principle of choosing the lesser harm.

Key Terms
ضرر عام (ḍarar 'āmm): Harm that affects the entire Muslim community, e.g., from an enemy fort
بَيْضَةُ الْإِسْلَامِ (bayḍat al-Islām): The core or stronghold of Islam; the Muslim community as a whole

A) It is prohibited under all circumstances.
B) It is permissible because the general benefit outweighs the specific harm.
C) It is permissible only if the prisoners are non-combatants.
D) It is obligatory even if it kills all prisoners.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits attacking enemy positions with Muslim captives based on the overriding principle of repelling general harm from the community of Islam.

Fighting Treaty-Breakers Without Prior Notice: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on treaty violation and notice requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a Muslim imam may fight treaty-breakers without notice and distinguish between a collective breach voiding the entire treaty and an isolated act that does not.

Core Idea
A treaty already broken by collective treachery requires no termination notice — the enemy nullified it themselves.

This lesson examines a key ruling from the Hanafi fiqh of siyar: when a Muslim imam may engage an enemy that has broken a treaty without prior notice. The ruling hinges on whether the breach was a collective act representing the whole nation or an isolated incident. We explore the distinction and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The source passage states that if the disbelievers themselves initiate treachery (khiyānah) by mutual agreement, the imam may fight them without giving notice (nabdh) of treaty termination.
This applies only when the breach is collective or with the king's permission.
2
Understand the condition: collective agreement
The breach must be by mutual agreement of the whole nation or with the explicit or implicit permission of their ruler. This makes the breach representative of the entire treaty party.
A small group acting without authority does not qualify.
3
Compare the exceptional case: isolated robbery
If a small, powerless group of disbelievers enters Dār al-Islām and commits robbery, this is not considered treaty-breaking by the entire nation. The treaty remains unaffected.
They are treated as thieves, not as agents of the state.
4
Analyze the intermediate case: powerful group without state backing
If a group has military power but likely acted without government consent, the imam may punish them individually (execute or enslave) but the treaty with the rest remains valid. If the government is implicated, it becomes collective treachery.
The default assumption is that the state is not responsible unless there is indication of state involvement.
5
Extract the underlying principle
The rationale (ta'līl) is that once the enemy has broken the covenant by their own action, it is no longer binding; therefore, no further notice of termination is required.
This is based on the nature of the treaty as a bilateral contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هفتم ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ اگر کافروں نے بد عہدی کرنے میں خود ہی ابتداء کی تو امام بھی ان سے مقابلہ کرے۔ اور معاہدہ کوختم کرنے کی ان کو اطلاع نہ دے اور ان کے پاس اس کی خبر نہ بھیجے بشرطیکہ ان کا فروں نے متفق ہو کر ویسا کیا ہو ( ۔ یا کافروں کی کسی بڑی جماعت نے اپنے بادشاہ کی اجازت سے خیانت کی ہو ) ۔ کیونکہ جب ان لوگوں نے خود ہی عہد توڑ دیا تو اب اس کے توڑنے کی ضرورت نہیں رہی بخلاف اس کے اگر کافروں کی ایک جماعت یا چھوٹی جماعت نے جن کو پوری قوت اور شوکت حاصل نہ ہو دار الاسلام میں گھس کر ڈکیتی کی تو اسے پوری قوم کا عہد توڑنا نہیں کہا جا سکتا ہے اور اگر ان لوگوں کو قوت حاصل ہو اور انہوں نے کھلم کھلا اعلانیہ مسلمانوں سے قتال کیا ہو تو یہ ان ڈکیتوں کے حق میں عہد شکنی شمار کی جائے گی لیکن پوری قوم کی طرف سے نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس کا یہ عمل اپنے بادشاہ کے مشورے اور اجازت کے بغیر ہوا ہے۔ اس لئے ان کا عمل دوسرے پر لازم نہ ہو گا ہاں اگر بادشاہ کی اجازت یا اس کے اشارہ سے کیا ہو تو یہ عہد شکنی سے
کی طرف سے ہوگی اور سب غدار کہلائیں گے کیونکہ وہ سب چھپ کر اس پر متفق پائے گئے۔
تشريح . قَالَ وَ إِنْ بَدَؤُا بِخِيَانَةٍ قَاتَلَهُمْ وَ لَمْ يَنبَذْ إِلَيْهِمْ إِذَا كَانَ ذَالِكَ بِاتِّفَاقِهِمْ لِأَنَّهُمْ صَارُ وَانًا قَضِيْنَ للعهد الخ۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر تھوڑے سے کافروں نے عہد کے خلاف مسلمانوں سے قتال کیا اگر واقعتا وہ اتنے تھوڑے آدمی ہوں جن کو مقابلہ کی طاقت نہیں تھی پھر بھی مقابلہ میں آئے تو انہیں چور سمجھا جائے گا اور معاہدہ پر اس کا اثر نہیں پڑے گا ۔ اور اگر ان کو مقابلہ کی طاقت ہو اور گمان غالب یہ ہو کہ انہوں نے اپنی حکومت کے اشارہ اور اجازت کے بغیر ایسا کیا ہے تو امام المسلمین کو یہ اختیار ہوگا کہ ان کو گرفتار کر کے چاہے قتل کر دے یا چاہے تو غلام بنا کر رکھ لے۔ لیکن باقی لوگوں سے معاہدہ حسب دستور باقی رہے گا اور اگر گمان الب یہ ہو کہ اپنی حکومت کے مشورے سے ایسا کیا ہے تو یہ غداری سب کی طرف سے سمجھی جائے گی۔
The Book of Siyar. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, volume seven. The translation of Quduri said: If the disbelievers themselves initiate treachery, then the imam should fight them, and he should not give them notice of terminating the treaty, nor send them news of it, provided that they did so by mutual agreement. Or if a large group of disbelievers committed treachery with the permission of their king. Because when they themselves broke the covenant, there is no need to break it. Unlike if a party of disbelievers or a small group who do not have full power and might entered Dar al-Islam and committed robbery, that cannot be considered breaking the treaty of the whole nation. And if those people have power and they openly fought the Muslims, then this will be considered breach of covenant for those robbers, but not on behalf of the whole nation. Because this action of theirs occurred without the advice and permission of their king. Therefore their action will not be binding on others. Yes, if it was done with the permission or indication of the king, then this will be considered breach of covenant on behalf of all, and all will be called traitors, because they all were found to have secretly agreed upon it. Commentary: He said: 'And if they initiate treachery, he may fight them without giving notice, if that is by their agreement, because they have become breakers of the covenant.' Summary: If a few disbelievers fought contrary to the treaty: if they were so few as to have no power to fight, yet they came to fight, they will be considered thieves, and the treaty will not be affected. And if they have power to fight and the predominant opinion is that they did so without indication and permission of their government, then the imam of the Muslims has the option to arrest them and either kill them or enslave them. But the treaty with the rest will remain as before. And if the predominant opinion is that they did so on the advice of their government, then this treachery will be considered on behalf of all.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Book of Siyar (conduct of war) in al-Hidayah, commented upon by Ashraf al-Hidayah. It deals with the situation where disbelievers with whom Muslims have a treaty break it. The main ruling: if the entire community of disbelievers collectively and openly breaches the treaty, the imam may fight them without giving prior notice of termination, because they themselves have already dissolved the covenant by their action. The passage distinguishes between a general breach by the whole nation (with the king's permission) and a localized breach by a small group acting independently. In the latter case, if the group is too weak to pose a real threat, their action is treated as robbery, not treaty-breaking by the entire nation. If they are powerful but act without government backing, the imam may punish them individually (execution or enslavement) but the treaty remains valid for the rest. Only if the government authorizes the breach does it become a collective betrayal, making all disloyal. The commentary uses the Arabic matn of Quduri (or Hidayah) and expands on the nuances: the key factor is whether the action represents the will of the entire polity or is an isolated incident. This follows Hanafi methodology of considering intent and effective cause (illa).

Key Terms
خيانة (khiyānah): Treachery or breach of trust in a treaty context
نبذ (nabdh): Throwing back (the treaty) i.e. formal notice of termination

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When may the imam fight the enemy without giving prior notice of treaty termination?
A) When the enemy collectively breaks the treaty with mutual agreement
B) Whenever the enemy commits any act of aggression
C) Only after a formal declaration of war
D) When the enemy is weak

Key Takeaway
A collective breach of treaty by the enemy nullifies the covenant, making notice of termination unnecessary.

Peace Treaty with Wealth: Conditions and Classification
Ruling on peace treaty with wealth payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a peace treaty with wealth and classify the wealth as jizyah or ghanimah.

Core Idea
Peace for wealth is permissible only when Muslims need it; wealth before battle is like jizyah, after encirclement it is ghanimah.

This lesson from the Hidayah addresses a crucial ruling in the law of jihad: can the imam accept wealth from the enemy in exchange for a truce? The answer depends on the Muslims' genuine need and the timing of the payment. We will examine the condition of need and how the method of acquisition determines whether the wealth is treated as jizyah (spent on public welfare) or ghanimah (divided among fighters).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
Determine what the imam is doing (making a truce) and the default permissibility of truces without wealth. The text states that a truce without wealth is permissible, so by analogy a truce with wealth is also permissible.
The default ruling is ja'iz (permissible) by qiyas on the permissibility of a truce without wealth.
2
Identify the condition of need
Note the condition that restricts this permissibility: the Muslims must be in need of wealth. Without need, the ruling becomes impermissible because jihad aims to elevate Allah's word, not worldly gain.
Need (hājah) is the operative condition; it turns a permissible act into a recommended or necessary one.
3
Distinguish the two scenarios: before and after encirclement
The text differentiates between when the enemy sends a messenger (no direct confrontation) and when the army surrounds them. In the first scenario, the wealth is like jizyah; in the second, it is ghanimah.
The key factor is whether the wealth was taken by force (even if via a treaty after encirclement) or by peaceful negotiation.
4
Classify the wealth: jizyah or ghanimah
If the truce is made without prior confrontation, the wealth is spent on the same categories as jizyah (public welfare). If the enemy is surrounded and then surrenders with wealth, it becomes ghanimah: one-fifth is set aside and the rest is distributed among the fighters.
This classification affects the distribution: jizyah goes to the state treasury, ghanimah includes a share for fighters.
5
Note the underlying legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The ruling is based on qiyas: since a truce without wealth is permissible, a truce with wealth is also permissible when needed. The wealth's classification is based on whether it is 'in the meaning of jizyah' (by analogy) or 'taken by force' (ghanimah).
Analogy (qiyas) and consideration of meaning (ma'na) are used to extend rulings.

Source Text

امام کیلئے مال کے عوض کفار سے صلح کا حکم
وَإِذَارَأَى الْإِمَامُ مُوَادَعَةَ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ وَ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ عَلَى ذَالِكَ مَا لا فَلَا بَأْسَ بِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا جَازَتِ الْمُوَادَعَهُ بِغَيْرِ الْمَالِ فَكَذَا بِالْمَالِ لكن هذا إذا
كَانَ بِالْمُسْلِمِينَ حَاجَةً أَمَّا إِذَا لَمْ تَكُنْ لَا يَجُوزُ لِمَا بَيْنَا مِنْ قَبْلُ وَالْمَاعُوذُ مِنَ الْمَالِ يُصْرَفُ مَصَارِفَ الْجِزْيَةِ هذَا إِذَا لَمْ يَنزِلُوا بِسَاحَتِهِمْ بَلْ أَرْسَلُوا رَسُولًا لِأَنَّهُ فِي مَعْنَى الْجِزْيَةِ أَمَّا إِذَا أَحَاطَ الْجَيْشُ بِهِمْ ثُمَّ أَخَذُوا الْمَالَ فَهُوَ غَيْمَةُ بِخَمْسِهَا وَتُقَسَّمُ الْبَاقِي بَيْنَهُمْ لِأَنَّهُ مَاعُوذُ بِالْفَهْرِ مَعْنى
ترجمہ اور اگر امام المسلمین نے کافروں سے مصالحت کرنے میں مصلحت سمجھی ساتھ ہی مال کے عوض صلح کرنے کو مناسب سمجھا تو اس میں بھی کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اس لئے صلح کے بدلہ مال لے سکتا ہے۔ بشرطیکہ واقعتا اس وقت مسلمانوں کو مال کی ضرورت اور مجبوری ہو ۔ اور اگر اس کی ضرورت نہ ہو تو جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس جہاد سے مقصود تو اللہ کا نام بلند کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ اور بغیر ضرورت مال لے کر جہاد کو ختم کر دینا جائز نہیں ہے البتہ ضرورت ہونے میں جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ صورت بھی معنی جہاد ہے۔ اس طرح جو کچھ مال ان سے لیا جائے گا اسے اس طرح اور اسی موقع میں خرچ کیا جائے گا ۔ جو جزیہ کے مال کے خرچ کی جگہ ہے ۔ اس مال میں جزیہ کا حکم اسی صورت میں ہو گا جبکہ مسلمانوں کے لشکر کا ان لوگوں سے آمنا سامنا نہ ہوا ہو۔ بلکہ صرف پیغام کے ذریعہ بات ملے ہو گئی ہو ۔ کیونکہ اس طرح حاصل کیا ہوا مال

Ruling on the imam making peace with disbelievers in exchange for wealth. And if the imam sees fit to make a truce with the people of war and to take wealth for that, there is no harm in it, because when a truce without wealth is permissible, so too with wealth. But this is when the Muslims have need. As for when there is no need, it is not permissible, due to what we have stated earlier. And the wealth taken is to be spent in the channels of jizyah. This is when they have not descended into their territory, but rather sent a messenger, because it is in the meaning of jizyah. But if the army surrounded them, then they took wealth, it is ghanimah: one-fifth of it is taken and the rest is divided among them, because it is wealth taken by force in meaning. Translation: And if the imam of the Muslims sees expediency in reconciling with the disbelievers, and also finds it appropriate to make peace in exchange for wealth, then there is no objection. Therefore he may take wealth in return for peace. Provided that at that time the Muslims actually have need and necessity for wealth. And if there is no need, it will not be permissible. Because the purpose of jihad is to elevate the name of Allah. And to end jihad by taking wealth without necessity is not permissible. However, when there is need, it is permissible, because this situation is also in the meaning of jihad. In this way, whatever wealth is taken from them will be spent in the same place and occasion, which is the place of expenditure of jizyah wealth. This wealth will have the ruling of jizyah only when the Muslim army has not confronted them face to face, but rather communication occurred only through a message. Because wealth obtained in this way will be in the meaning of jizyah. And if the Muslims surrounded them, and then they made peace out of helplessness, then this wealth will be considered ghanimah: that is, make five shares of that wealth, keep one share, and distribute the remaining four shares among the mujahideen. Because in this way they took wealth and subdued them. Because the disbelievers gave wealth and made peace while being compelled and subdued. And since the Muslims had need for wealth, the imam accepted this peace, so this wealth will also be considered ghanimah wealth, just as when they subdue them after actual and real fighting and obtain ghanimah wealth from them. Commentary: And if the imam sees... the meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Book of Siyar regarding the permissibility of the imam making a peace treaty with hostile disbelievers (ahl al-harb) in exchange for wealth. The ruling is conditional: it is only permissible when the Muslims have a genuine need for wealth (e.g., for defense or welfare). Without need, it is not allowed because the primary objective of jihad is to elevate Allah's word, not worldly gain. The passage also details the classification of the wealth received: if the peace is made before military confrontation (through negotiation), the wealth is treated like jizyah (poll tax) and spent accordingly. If the Muslims have already surrounded the enemy and then they surrender offering wealth, that wealth is considered ghanimah (spoils of war), subject to khums (one-fifth) and distribution to the fighters. The commentary clarifies that this distinction is based on whether the wealth is obtained by force (even if through a treaty after encirclement) or by peaceful agreement beforehand. The Hanafi position emphasizes the intention and context: jihad is primarily for da'wah, but need may necessitate accepting wealth.

Key Terms
موادعة (muwāda‘ah): Truce or peace treaty with non-Muslims
جزيہ (jizyah): Per capita tax paid by dhimmis; here the wealth taken by treaty before combat is analogous to jizyah
غنيمت (ghanīmah): Spoils of war taken by force; here wealth taken after encirclement is ghanimah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the Muslim army has surrounded the enemy and the enemy offers wealth for peace, the wealth is classified as:
A) Jizyah
B) Ghanimah
C) Sadaqah
D) Fay'

Key Takeaway
A peace treaty with wealth is permissible only when Muslims need the wealth; the classification of the wealth depends on whether it is taken before or after military encirclement.

Peace with Apostates: No Wealth, Only Hope
Ruling on peace with apostates: no wealth taken, delay allowed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making peace with apostates and explain why wealth cannot be taken.

Core Idea
Peace with apostates is allowed but not for wealth — jizyah is impermissible from apostates.

When apostates establish themselves as an independent power, the imam may choose peace to give them a chance to return to Islam. This lesson examines the limits of such a peace agreement, distinguishing apostates from original disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making peace (ṣulḥ) with apostates (murtaddūn) who have formed an independent territory. The ruling is that it is permissible (jāʾiz) for the imam to make peace with them, but without taking any wealth.
This is unlike peace with original disbelievers, where wealth may be taken.
2
Locate the dalīl
The evidence cited in the text is the hope (rajāʾ) that apostates may return to Islam, which justifies delaying fighting. Additionally, the practice of Caliph ʿUthmān is mentioned: he ordered that followers of Musaylimah al-Kadhdhāb be called to Islam, and those who repented were spared.
The story of ʿUthmān is a sunnah/precedent from the Rightly-Guided Caliphs.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The hope of Islam indicates that the priority is to encourage repentance, not to extract wealth. The prohibition of jizyah from apostates (as will be detailed in the chapter of jizyah) prevents the imam from taking any payment for peace.
The key legal link: apostates are not eligible for jizyah, so any peace conditioned on wealth would be invalid.
4
Note the intra-Hanafī ikhtilāf
Abū Ḥanīfa, Abū Yūsuf (in one narration), and Muḥammad all agree that the imam should demand repentance (tawbah) from apostates before fighting. There is no dispute among them on the permissibility of peace without wealth.
The muftā bihī is that repentance must be called for.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab status
Some other schools may allow delaying peace or taking wealth, but the Ḥanafī position is that jizyah is not permissible from apostates, so peace must be free of payment.
This distinction is critical for muʿāmalāt with apostate groups.

Source Text

Ruling on making peace with apostates. And as for the apostates, the imam may make peace with them so that they may consider their affair, because Islam is hoped from them. So it is permissible to delay fighting them out of hope for their Islam. And he should not take wealth for it, because taking jizyah from them is not permissible, as will be explained. Translation: And those people who apostatized from Islam (then gained dominance over some territory and became independent until that territory took the form of dar al-harb. But later they requested peace from the imam, and the imam also considered peace expedient at that time), then the imam may make peace with them, so that he may consider their matter. Because there remains hope that these apostates may become Muslims again. So on this hope, delaying fighting them is permissible. And wealth cannot be taken for making peace with them (even though wealth can be taken for peace with disbelievers, because taking jizyah from apostates is not permissible. Its detail will be explained in the chapter of jizyah, insha'Allah). Commentary: Discussion on delaying fighting due to hope of acceptance of Islam. In this case, hope of acceptance of Islam means demanding repentance from apostates. Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf (according to one narration) and Imam Muhammad say that the leader of the Muslim army should demand repentance from the apostate; it is better. In case of refusal to repent, the apostate should be killed. It is narrated from 'Ubaydullah bin 'Abdullah bin 'Uqbah that some people were arrested in Kufa while they were propagating the falsehoods of Musaylimah al-Kadhdhab. He (Abdullah) wrote to 'Uthman (the caliph) about them (the followers of Musaylimah). Upon this, 'Uthman wrote back: Present to them the true religion and the Shahada; whoever accepts and abandons Musaylimah al-Kadhdhab, do not kill him; and whoever adheres to the false religion of Musaylimah al-Kadhdhab, kill him. It should be clear that in the present age, this same ruling applies to the fitnah of Qadianism, Agha Khanism, Rafidah, Baha'iism. Because these people also believe in the prophethood (literally or in meaning) of Ghulam Ahmad Qadiani, Agha Khan, the Twelve Imams, and Muhammad Baha' etc., and are insistent and busy in their propagation. ... 'Abdullah bin Mas'ud arrested those who believed in the prophethood of Musaylimah al-Kadhdhab; some of them repented regarding Musaylimah...
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on apostates (murtaddun) who have established an independent territory. The imam is permitted to make peace with them, not for wealth, but to allow time for them to return to Islam. The key point: unlike with original disbelievers (ahl al-harb), the imam cannot take jizyah or any wealth from apostates because apostates are required to either return to Islam or be killed; their acceptance of wealth would not signify submission to Islamic rule. The commentary discusses the imam's option to delay fighting in hope of their repentance, citing the practice of the Companions. It extends this ruling to contemporary heretical groups that claim prophethood, such as Qadianis and Baha'is. The Hanafi position emphasizes that apostates are to be called to repentance (tawbah) before execution, as stated by Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): One who apostatizes from Islam and may establish a separate territory
توبہ (tawbah): Repentance; here it means returning to Islam, demanded before execution

Apostates are not eligible for jizyah, so peace with them cannot include any payment; they must be called to repentance.

No Money from Apostates in Peace Treaty
Ruling on impermissibility of accepting money in peace with apostates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking wealth in peace treaties with apostates and explain the legal reasoning.

Core Idea
Taking wealth from apostates in a peace treaty is haram because it functions like jizya, which is impermissible from apostates.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in the law of apostasy (ahkam al-murtaddin). The Hanafi school holds that even in dire situations, an imam cannot accept money from apostates to end hostilities. Why? Because apostates' property lacks legal protection (mal mutaqawwim) and accepting payment amounts to jizya, which is invalid from those who have forsaken Islam. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the limits of necessity (darura) and the unique legal status of apostates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The passage describes a situation where apostates overwhelm Muslims. The ruling is that peace is permitted out of necessity, but taking wealth from them is not allowed.
The ruling has two parts: peace allowed, payment forbidden.
2
Analyze the first reason: mal mutaqawwim
Apostates' property is not considered protectable (mal mutaqawwim) because they themselves are not under Islamic protection. Therefore, accepting wealth from them has no legal basis.
This is a key distinction from the property of dhimmis.
3
Analyze the second reason: analogy to jizya
Receiving money in exchange for peace is analogized to jizya (poll tax). Jizya is only taken from non-Muslims who remain on their original religion, not from apostates.
The purpose of jizya is to allow dhimmis to practice their faith; apostates have no such right.
4
Understand the usul: qiyas and istihsan
The ruling is derived by qiyas: sulh bi-mal is like jizya. The text notes this analogy can be overridden by istihsan in extreme necessity, but the prohibition on payment remains strict.
Istihsan would not permit payment because it would effectively endorse apostasy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرتدوں سے مال کے عوض صلح کا عدم جواز
اگر دوران قتال ( لڑائی ) لشکر اسلام پر مرتدین کا غلبہ ہو جائے اور مجاہدین اسلام سمیت عام مسلمانوں کی قتل و غارت کا واضح حال سامنے آجائے تو اس صورت میں از روئے مصلحت مرتدوں سے صلح کرنے کی اجازت ہے۔ لیکن ان ( مرتدوں ) سے مال کو بطور معاوضہ حاصل نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ (۱) ان ( مرتدوں ) کامل متقوم ( قیمتی ) نہیں جو کہ اسلام کے شایان شان نہیں ۔ ( صلح بعوض مال معنوی طور پر جزیہ ہے اور مرتدوں سے جزیہ اخذ کرنا جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ کفار سے جزیہ وصول کرنے کا مقصد انہیں
The impermissibility of peace in exchange for wealth with apostates. If during fighting (battle) the Muslims are overwhelmed by the apostates and the killing and destruction of mujahideen and general Muslims becomes apparent, then in that situation, due to maslaha, peace with apostates is permitted. But wealth as a consideration shall not be taken from them because (1) their wealth is not protected (mal mutaqawwim) which is not befitting for Islam. (Peace in exchange for wealth is essentially jizya, and taking jizya from apostates is not permissible. Because the purpose of taking jizya from disbelievers is to...
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage continues the ruling on apostates, focusing on a specific scenario: when apostates overwhelm Muslims during battle, peace may be made out of necessity. However, even then, the Imam cannot accept money from them in return for peace. The reasoning is twofold: First, the apostates' wealth is not considered protected property (mal mutaqawwim) under Islamic law; they themselves and their property are not entitled to protection due to their apostasy. Second, accepting wealth as a consideration for peace is analogous to jizya, and jizya is not permissible from apostates. Jizya is taken from non-Muslims who remain on their original religion, not from those who left Islam. The text ends mid-sentence, explaining that the purpose of jizya is to... (likely continue: to allow them to remain on their religion under Muslim protection, which does not apply to apostates). This ruling underscores the Hanafi principle that apostates do not have the status of dhimmis, and their blood and property are not inviolable unless they repent.

Key Terms
مال متقوم (mal mutaqawwim): Property that is legally protected and has value in Islamic law; apostates' property is not mutaqawwim due to their status.
صلح (sulh): A peace treaty or settlement; in this context, a truce ending hostilities.
جزیہ (jizya): A poll tax paid by non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in exchange for protection and freedom of religion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it impermissible to take wealth from apostates in a peace treaty?
A) Because they are poor
B) Because apostates' property is not protected (non-mutaqawwim)
C) Because the imam cannot make peace
D) Because war must continue

Key Takeaway
Taking money from apostates in peace treaties is prohibited because it functions as jizya, which is only for those who remain on their original religion.

Calling Apostates to Islam Before Execution
Companion practices establishing the sunnah of three calls

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah of calling apostates to Islam three times before fighting and identify the Companion precedents that establish this rule.

Core Idea
Apostates must be called to Islam three times before execution.

The Hanafi school derives the procedure for dealing with apostates from the actions of the Companions, particularly Ali ibn Abi Talib and Umar ibn al-Khattab. This lesson examines two incidents that establish the sunnah of offering the apostate multiple opportunities to repent before any punitive action is taken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Companion incidents
Read the passage and separate the narration of Bara' from the story of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and the apostates of Majiba. Note the key actions of Ali and Umar.
Ali sent Bara' to Nahrawan; Abu Musa conquered Kasr and killed apostates joined with polytheists.
2
Extract the ruling from each incident
From Ali’s incident: the apostates were called three times. From Umar’s statement: he would have presented the door of Islam (called them back) and only imprisoned if they refused. Conclude that calling is the preferred practice.
Umar did not punish the killers, showing that killing apostates who refuse is permitted but the sunnah is to call first.
3
Apply the Hanafi legal classification
Determine that the three calls are a sunnah (recommended act), not a wajib (obligatory). The killing is valid without calls, but the better practice is to invite.
The term 'sunnah' here means the established practice of the Companions, not necessarily a binding requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حضرت براء رضی اللہ عنہ سے مروی ہے کہ حضرت علی المرتضیٰ نے ان کو اہل نہروان کی طرف بھیجا تو انہوں (حضر، براٹی) نے اہل نہروان کو تین بار اسلام کی دعوت دی۔
حضرت ابو موسیٰ اشعری نے مقام کسر فتح کر کے تجیبہ کے ان مرتدوں کو قتل کر دیا جو مشرکین سے مل گئے تھے۔ ان کے بارے میں حضرت عمرؓ نے حضرت انس بن مالک سے گفتگو کرتے وقت فرمایا کہ اگر میں (عمر بن خطاب ) انہیں زندہ گرفتار کر لیتا تو ان پر وہ دروازہ (اسلام ) پیش کرتا جس سے وہ نکلے تھے۔ اگر وہ (مجیبہ کے مرتد ) لوٹ آتے تو ٹھیک ورنہ میں انہیں قید کر دیتا۔ البتہ حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ جیبہ کے مرتدوں کو قتل کرنے کی پاداش میں قاتلوں سے کوئی مواخذہ نہیں کیا۔
It is narrated from Hadrat Bara' (may Allah be pleased with him) that Hadrat Ali al-Murtada sent him to the people of Nahrawan, and he called the people of Nahrawan to Islam three times. Hadrat Abu Musa al-Ash'ari conquered the place of Kasr and killed those apostates of Majiba who had joined the polytheists. Regarding them, Hadrat Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said while speaking to Hadrat Anas ibn Malik: 'If I had captured them alive, I would have presented them with the door (of Islam) through which they had exited. If they returned, it would be fine; otherwise I would have imprisoned them.' However, Hadrat Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) did not hold the killers accountable for killing the apostates of Majiba.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling_statement derived from the practice of the Companions regarding the treatment of apostates before engaging in combat. The narration from Bara' indicates that Ali (ra) instructed him to call the people of Nahrawan (a group of apostates) to Islam three times. This establishes a sunnah: apostates must be given multiple opportunities to repent before any military action. The incident of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and the apostates of Majiba shows that Umar (ra) approved of killing apostates who had joined the polytheists, but he preferred to first offer them a chance to return to Islam. Umar's statement that he would have 'presented them with the door through which they had exited' metaphorically means he would have invited them back to the faith they left. He would not have executed them outright unless they refused. Furthermore, Umar did not punish those who killed these apostates, indicating that killing apostates who persist in their apostasy and join the enemy is permissible without penalty. However, the preferred course is to call them to Islam first.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A person who has left Islam after being a Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many times did Hadrat Ali instruct Bara' to call the people of Nahrawan to Islam?
A) Once
B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Seven times

Key Takeaway
Apostates should be called to Islam three times before any execution, following the sunnah of the Companions.
