Repentance of Repeated Apostates Not Accepted
Quranic verse and ruling on repeated apostates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the repentance of repeated apostates and explain the Quranic evidence from Surah An-Nisa 4:137.

Core Idea
Repeated apostasy blocks forgiveness: Allah explicitly rejects repentance.

This lesson addresses a strict ruling: a person who repeatedly converts and reconverts to Islam, steadily increasing in disbelief, will not have their repentance accepted. The proof is a clear Quranic verse. We will unpack the ruling, its evidence, and its implications in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (repentance of a repeated apostate) and the exact legal consequence (not accepted).
The act is tawbah (repentance); the ruling is non-acceptance.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the specific proof cited: Quran 4:137. Notice the verse describes a pattern of belief, disbelief, belief, disbelief, then increased disbelief.
The verse ends with لَّمْ يَكُنِ اللَّهُ لِيَغْفِرَ لَهُمْ (Allah will not forgive them).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Analyze how the verse proves the ruling. The negation of forgiveness ('will not forgive') directly implies that repentance is not accepted. The context specifies repeated apostasy.
Hanafi usul: the negated form gives a clear prohibition of acceptance.
4
Identify the Scope
Note that this ruling applies specifically to those who repeatedly apostatize and increase in disbelief, not to a first-time apostate who sincerely repents.
Common misunderstanding: it applies to all apostates, but the text limits it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جولوگ بار بار مرتد ہو جائیں اور پھر کفر میں بڑھ جائیں تو ایسے مرتدوں کی توبہ قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ قرآن مجید میں مذکور ہے کہ : اِنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا ثُمَّ كَفَرُوا ثُمَّ امَنُوا ثُمَّ كَفَرُوا ثَمَّ ازْدَادُوا كُفْرًا لَّمْ يَكُنِ اللَّهُ لِيَغْفِرَ لَهُمُ الآية (النساء: ۱۳۷) بلاشبہ جولوگ ایمان لائے پھر کا فر ہو گئے پھر ایمان لائے پھر کفر کیا پھر کفر میں بڑھ گئے ان کی تو بہ ہرگز قبول نہ ہوگی۔ ( کما جاء فی الطحاوی)
Those people who repeatedly become apostate and then increase in disbelief, the repentance of such apostates will not be accepted. Because it is mentioned in the Noble Quran: 'Indeed, those who have believed then disbelieved, then believed then disbelieved, then increased in disbelief – never will Allah forgive them...' (An-Nisa 4:137). Undoubtedly, those who believed then disbelieved, then believed then disbelieved, then increased in disbelief, their repentance will never be accepted. (As it has come in al-Tahawi)
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof. It states a strict ruling: an apostate who repeatedly converts and reconverts, and persists in disbelief, will not have his repentance accepted by Allah. The proof is the explicit Quranic verse (4:137). The wording 'لَّمْ يَكُنِ اللَّهُ لِيَغْفِرَ لَهُمُ' indicates that Allah will not forgive them. This means that even if such a person outwardly returns to Islam, their repentance is not accepted in the sense that they are not to be trusted, and they face eternal punishment. However, Hanafi scholars discuss the practical implications: such a person may still be required to repent to avoid execution, but their repentance is deemed insincere. The ruling is based on the verse and is supported by the authority of al-Tahawi. This is a clear-cut ruling that leaves no room for leniency towards habitual apostates.

Key Terms
توبہ (tawbah): Repentance and return to Islam from apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A hadith from the Prophet
B) Surah An-Nisa 4:137
C) Consensus of the companions
D) Analogy to other crimes

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the repentance of a person who repeatedly apostatizes and persists in disbelief is not accepted, based on the explicit Quranic verse 4:137.

Peace with Apostates: The Rule of Non-Protected Wealth
Ruling on apostates' wealth and exception for enemy siege.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking wealth from apostates in a peace agreement and explain the basis of 'mal ghayr ma'sum'.

Core Idea
Apostate wealth is non-protected; taking it is makruh tahrimi but once taken, it is not returned.

This lesson addresses a specific siyar (international law) issue: peace with apostates. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the ruling on the act of making peace for wealth and the status of the wealth once taken. Understanding the concept of 'mal ghayr ma'sum' is key to grasping the legal logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, note the two scenarios: (1) imam makes peace with apostates in exchange for wealth; (2) enemy besieges Muslims and demands payment for truce. For the former, the act is makruh tahrimi (prohibited), but if done, the wealth is not returned because it is non-protected. For the latter, paying is prohibited unless there is fear of destruction.
The passage does not state the first ruling as haram explicitly but derives from the reasoning that apostate wealth is non-protected.
2
Understand 'mal ghayr ma'sum'
The key concept is 'mal ghayr ma'sum' (non-protected wealth). This refers to property that lacks inviolability under Islamic law, such as the property of apostates, because they have forfeited their right to ownership by leaving Islam. Therefore, taking it does not constitute a wrongful taking that must be remedied.
Compare with 'mal ma'sum' (protected wealth) of Muslims and dhimmis.
3
Apply the exception for enemy siege
In the second scenario, the enemy's wealth is protected (since they are not Muslims but are in a non-Muslim territory? Actually the text doesn't say enemy's wealth, it says the Muslims pay. The ruling is that the imam should not agree because it involves humiliation and paying diyah. However, if destruction is feared, it becomes obligatory to pay to save lives, even if it means giving wealth.
This exception is based on the principle that necessity overrides prohibition.
4
Note the practical implication
In practice, if an imam makes a peace deal with apostates for wealth, the wealth is considered fay' (booty) and need not be returned. This encourages strong stance against apostasy while providing a legal solution if such a deal occurs.
This ruling is specific to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ أَخَذَهُ لَمْ يَرُدَّهُ لِأَنَّهُ مَال غَيْرُ مَعْصُومٍ وَلَوْ حَاصَرَ الْعَدُرُّ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَطَلَبُوا الْمَوَادَعَةَ عَلَى مَالٍ يَدْفَعُهُ المُسْلِمُونَ إِلَيْهِمْ لَا يَفْعَلُ الْإِمَامُ لِمَافِيهِ مِنْ إِعْطَاءِ الدَيَّةِ وَإِلْحَاقِ الْمَذَلَّةِ بِأَهْلِ الْإِسْلَامِ إِلَّا إِذَا خَافَ الْهَلَاكَ لِأَنَّ دَفْعَ الْهَلَاكِ وَاحِبُ بِأي طَرِيقٍ يُمْكِنُ
And if he (the imam) takes it (wealth from apostates in peace), he will not return it, because it is wealth without immunity. And if the enemy besieges the Muslims and they request a truce for wealth that the Muslims pay to them, the imam should not do it due to what it involves of giving blood money and bringing humiliation upon the people of Islam, unless he fears destruction, because repelling destruction is obligatory by any means possible.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage provides two related rulings. First: If the imam makes a peace agreement with apostates in exchange for wealth (i.e., the apostates pay to avoid fighting), and he actually takes the wealth, he is not required to return it later. The reason is that an apostate's wealth is 'ghayr ma'sum' (non-protected), meaning it is not considered sacred or inviolable because the apostate has lost the right to own property by leaving Islam. Therefore, taking it is permissible, and once taken, it is like booty. Second: If the enemy (kuffar) besieges the Muslims and demands payment for a truce, the imam should not agree because that would involve paying blood money (diyah) and would humiliate the Muslims. However, if there is a real fear of total destruction (halak), then the imam may pay to avoid annihilation, since preserving life is obligatory by any available means. The underlying rationale (talil) is that the apostate's property is not protected, whereas the enemy's property is protected? Actually the second case involves the enemy's demand, not payment from them. The ruling here balances between avoiding humiliation and necessity.

Key Terms
مال غیر معصوم (maal ghayr ma'sum): Wealth that is not protected by Islamic law, i.e., without inviolability; can be taken without liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the apostates are enemies and have no rights
B) Because the wealth is non-protected (ghayr ma'sum)
C) Because the wealth was given willingly
D) Because the imam needs the wealth for the treasury

Key Takeaway
Apostate wealth is non-protected; taking it in a peace agreement is not recommended but if taken, it is not returned.

Loss of Apostate's Ownership: Causes and Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether apostasy itself causes loss of ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the cause of loss of ownership for an apostate and apply the mufta bihi view in a case of repentance.

Core Idea
Apostasy alone ends ownership according to Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn require death or joining dar al-harb.

This lesson explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the moment an apostate loses ownership of his property. While both sides agree that apostasy is a cause, they differ on whether it is sufficient on its own or whether a further event like death is required. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the ruling on apostate property in cases of repentance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two causes of loss of ownership
From the passage, note that loss of ownership occurs due to (1) death, killing, or joining dar al-harb, and (2) apostasy. This sets the stage for the dispute.
2
State the position of the Sahibayn
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, apostasy alone does not terminate ownership; it only ends upon death, execution, or joining enemy territory.
They consider the possibility of repentance and restoration of rights.
3
Infer Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Although the text does not explicitly state his view, the structure implies that Abu Hanifa holds apostasy itself to be a sufficient cause, analogizing it to civil death.
His dalil is qiyas with death.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if an apostate repents before death, according to Sahibayn his property is restored; according to Abu Hanifa it is not, having already been forfeited.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi fatwa adopted the Sahibayn's view because it is more lenient and encourages repentance.
This is the operative ruling in most Hanafi contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زوال ملکیت کے اسباب دو ہیں، (1) موت قتل، دار الحرب سے ملنا۔ (۲) ترک اسلام یعنی ارتداد ۔ چنانچہ زوال ملکیت کے اسباب کے حوالے سے امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین (امام ابو یوسف، امام محمد ) کے درمیان اختلاف پایا جاتا ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ مرتد کا زوال ملکیت ارتداد کی بناء پر تحقیق نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مرتد کا مال پر سے ملکیت کا خاتمہ موت یا قتل یا دار الحرب میں مل جانے
There are two causes for the loss of ownership: (1) death, killing, or joining dar al-harb. (2) Leaving Islam, i.e., apostasy. Regarding the causes of loss of ownership, there is a difference of opinion between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad). The Sahibayn say that the loss of ownership of an apostate does not occur based on apostasy; rather, the termination of ownership over his wealth occurs through death, killing, or joining dar al-harb.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. It identifies two causes for the loss of an apostate's ownership of property: (1) death (whether natural or execution) and joining dar al-harb (enemy territory), and (2) apostasy itself. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that apostasy alone does not cause loss of ownership; the apostate retains ownership of his property until he dies, is killed, or joins dar al-harb. Imam Abu Hanifa's view (implied by the structure) is that apostasy itself immediately terminates ownership, making his wealth like booty. The practical difference: according to Abu Hanifa, the apostate's property can be seized immediately upon apostasy; according to the Sahibayn, it remains his until a later event. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school is often that of the Sahibayn in such matters, but this must be verified against other sources. The passage indicates the ikhtilaf is well-known.

Key Terms
زوال ملکیت (zawaal al-milkiyyah): Loss of ownership or legal possession of property.
صاحبین (al-sahibayn): The two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, major students of Abu Hanifa.
مرتد (murtadd): An apostate; one who leaves Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately upon apostasy
B) Only upon death, execution, or joining dar al-harb
C) After a year of apostasy
D) Never, even after death

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that an apostate does not lose ownership of his property by apostasy alone; loss occurs only upon death or joining dar al-harb.

Invalidity of Aman from Muslim Prisoners and Merchants in Dar al-Harb
Ruling with rational proofs on aman from captive Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of aman from a Muslim prisoner or merchant in dar al-harb and apply the condition that the granter must inspire fear.

Core Idea
A Muslim under enemy control cannot grant aman — only those who inspire fear may do so.

In the law of war (siyar), aman (safe conduct) is a critical instrument for Muslim security. But not every Muslim can validly grant it. This lesson examines a key ruling from Al-Hidayah: the aman of a Muslim prisoner or merchant in enemy territory is invalid. The reasoning rests on a simple yet profound principle: aman is only effective from one whom the enemy fears. Let's explore why the captive and the trader fall short.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
First, locate the direct ruling: is the aman of a Muslim prisoner or merchant valid? The text states it is not acceptable (ghayr jaa'iz / batil).
The ruling is absolute — no exception for necessity.
2
Analyse the core condition for valid aman
The text repeatedly states that aman is 'specific to a place of fear' (mahall al-khawf). The granter must be a source of fear to the enemy. Why? Because only such a person can genuinely guarantee safety.
This is a rational (aqli) condition derived from the purpose of aman.
3
Apply the condition to the prisoner/merchant
Assess whether a prisoner or trader in dar al-harb inspires fear. The text says no — they are under enemy control, helpless, and dependent. Therefore, they fail the condition.
Even if the prisoner is brave, his captivity negates the perception of threat.
4
Examine the supplementary proofs
The text offers two rational proofs: (1) The enemy can force them to grant aman under duress, so the aman is not truly voluntary. (2) Accepting such aman would let the enemy escape pressure and block future conquests.
These are istihsani (juristic preference) arguments supporting the core condition.
5
Extend the ruling to related cases
The passage also mentions a Muslim who converts in dar al-harb but does not migrate — his aman is also invalid. Why? Same reason: he remains under enemy authority and does not inspire fear.
Extension reinforces that the condition applies to anyone lacking independent power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير
اور یہ بھی کہا ہے کہ جو مسلمان ان کافروں کے قبضہ میں اور ان کے قیدی ہیں یا امان لے کر ان کافروں کے پاس تجارت کی غرض سے موجود ہوں اس قیدی یا تاجر کا بھی امان دینا ان حربیوں اور کافروں کے حق میں قابل قبول نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ دونوں ان کافروں کے اختیار اور قبضہ میں ہیں اس لئے کفار کو ان سے کوئی خطرہ اور خوف نہیں ہے۔ جبکہ امان اسی شخص کی قابل قبول ہوتی ہے جس سے کسی کو خطرہ اور خوف ہو ۔ یعنی کفار کو جس سے خوف ہو گا اسی کی امان صحیح ہو گی ۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ کفار تو ان دونوں پر امان دینے اور امان لکھنے پر جبر بھی کر سکتے ہیں۔ لہذا ایسی امان مسلمانوں کی مصلحت سے خارج ہو گی ۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ اگر قیدی یا تاجر کی دی ہوئی امان کو قبول کر لینا صحیح ہو جائے تو جب کبھی بھی حربیوں پر مسلمانوں کی طرف سے سخت ہوگی وہ کسی مسلمان قیدی یا تاجر کو پکڑ کر بلکہ سی تو اکثر ان کے پاس رہ بھی سکتے ہیں۔ ان سے امان لے کر چھوٹ جائیں گے اور نتیجہ یہ ہو گا کہ مجاہدین پر ان کفار کو فتح کر لینے کا دروازہ ہمیشہ کے لئے بند ہو جائے گا۔ اور جو شخص دار الحرب میں مسلمان ہو گیا مگر وہاں سے ہجرت کر کے دارالاسلام میں نہیں آیا تو اس کا امان دینا بھی صحیح نہ ہوگا (کیونکہ ان کفار کو اس شخص سے کچھ بھی خوف و خطرہ نہیں ہوگا حالانکہ امان کا صحیح ہونا اسی شخص کے لئے مخصوص ہے جس سے امان چاہنے والے کو خطرہ بھی ہو ۔ واضح ہو کہ اجازت دینے والے غلام کی یہ دو صورتیں ہو سکتی ہیں۔ نمبرا۔ یا تو وہ مجبور ہوگا یعنی اس کے مالک کی طرف سے اسے کسی قسم کا معاملہ اور کاروبار کرنے کی اجازت نہ ہو نمبر ۔ اور یاوہ ماذون ہو گا یعنی اس کے مولی نے اسے کاروبار اور قتال کرنے کی اجازت دے دی ہو۔ ان دونوں کے درمیان حکم کے اعتبار سے کچھ فرق ہے جسے مصنف نے عبادت سے بیان کیا ہے)۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جو مسلمان کفار کے پاس قیدی یا امن لے کر ان کے یہاں تجارت کی غرض سے گیا تو اس قیدی یا تاجر کا حربیوں کے حق میں امان دینا جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ مسلمان قیدی یا تاجر کفار کی ماتحتی میں قہر زدہ ہیں۔ امان محل خوف سے مخصوص ہوتی ہے اڈوہ خوف اہل کفر می موجود نہیں۔ یعنی اہل کفر کو جس سے خوف ہوتا ہے اس کی امان کا جواز موجود ہوتا ہے۔ بائیں دلیل کہ کفار قیدی یا تاجر پر زبردستی امان طلب کریں گے۔ یوں امان دینے کا عمل خارج از مصلحت ہو جائے گا۔ اگر کفار قیدی یا تاجر پالیس تو ان (قیدی ، تاجر ) سے امان کی آڑ میں چھٹکارا حاصل کر لیں گے۔ تو درمیں صورت اہل اسلام کے حق میں فتوحات کا دروازہ نہیں کھلتا امان کے جواز میں اصول یہ ہے کہ امان دینے سے قبل قوت و ضعف پر مبنی خفیہ حالات پر غور کیا جائے۔ اگر دار الاسلام یا میدان کارزار میں موجود مجاہدین اسلام امان کی پیش کش کے وقت طاقتور ہیں اور کفار کیلئے ضرر رسانی ناممکن ہو تو امان دینا صحیح اقدام متصور ہوگا اور بصورت دیگر پناہ دینے سے اہل کفر نقصان دے سکتے ہیں۔ چنانچہ اندرونی طور پر ضعف پر مبنی حالات امان دینے کے مقتضی نہیں ہوتے لہذا امان دینے کا اصول یہی ہے کہ دار الاسلام مجاہدین اسلام کے اندرون خانہ حالات پر نظر کی جائے۔ اس سے یہ واضح ہوتا ہے کہ کوئی بھی مسلمان اس وقت تک کافروں کو امان دینے کا استحقاق نہیں رکھتا جب تک وہ دار الاسلام یا اہل کفر سے برسر پیکار مجاہدین کے اندرونی مخفی حالات سے بخوبی باخبر نہ ہو۔
- چونکہ کفار کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان یا اہل کفر کے ملک میں موجود مسلمان تاجر دار الاسلام اور مجاہدین کے خفیہ حالات سے بے خبر ہوتا ہے اس لئے قیدی یا تاجر کی دی ہوئی امان نا قابل تسلیم ہوگی۔
مسلمان قیدی ہو یا تاجر ہر دو کفار کے قبضہ میں ہوتے ہیں۔ کفار انہیں (مسلم قیدی ، تاجر کو ) جس طرح چاہیں استعمال کرنے کے مختار ہیں۔ مبادا کہ ان ( مسلمان قیدی یا تاجر ) کی آڑ میں اہل اسلام کے لئے نقصان دہ ثابت ہوں۔ چنانچہ کفار کے ضرر سے محفوظ رہتے کیلئے یہ امرضروری قرار پایا کہ کفار کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان یا دل الحرب میں موجود تاجر کی امان کو نا قابل قبول قرار دیا جائے تا کہ کفر کی فریب کاریوں اور عیارانہ چالوں کو ناکامی کا سامنا ہو اور تمام مسلمان ان کے شر اور نقصان سے محفوظ ہوسکیں ۔ ۴۔ امان کے ارکان میں سے ایک رکن یہ ہے کہ امان دینے والا شخص آزاد ہو جب کہ کفار کی قید میں محبوس آدمی اگر چہ مسلمان اور بنیادی طور پر آزاد ہوتا ہے لیکن کفار کے قبضہ میں آنے کے باعث وہ فی الوقت مجبور محض ہو جاتا ہے۔ بایں وجہ کہ وہ ( مسلمان قیدی ) ہمہ تن کفار کے رحم و کرم پر ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ قیدی کی وقتی اسارت (قید) کے پیش نظر اسے ( مسلمان قیدی کو امان دینے کے قابل نہیں سمجھا جاتا۔ یہی حال اس مسلمان تاجر کا ہے جو دار الحرب ( مملکت کفریہ ) میں تجارتی ضرورتوں اور دار الاسلام کی سرحد سے کوسوں دور ہونے کی وجہ ہے اہل کفر کامحتاج ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا مسلمان قیدی اور دار الحرب میں مسلمان تاجر کفار کے مد مقابل مجبور و مقہور ہونے کے باعث اہل اسلام کو امان دینے کی لیاقت نہیں رکھتا۔ ۵- از روی مصلحت امان محل خوف کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ یعنی کفار ہمیشہ ایسے مسلمان سے خائف ہوتے ہیں جو صاحب قتال وذی عقل اور آزادی پر مبنی صفات سے متصف ہو۔ کیونکہ اہل قبال نہ صرف ہمیشہ مسلح رہتا ہے بلکہ کفار کو سرنگوں کرنے کے عمل میں ہر وقت مصروف رہتا ہے۔ چنانچہ اہل قتال کی صفت کا حامل مسلمان کفار کی مرعوبیت کا باعث ہی نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ہر وقت ان (کفار ) پر مسلمان اہل قتال کا خوف بھی طاری رہتا ہے۔ جب کہ کفار کا قیدی (مسلمان) اہل کفر کے دلوں میں ذرہ بھر خوف طاری نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ وہ (مسلمان قید یا دار الحرب میں موجود تا جر ) خوف طاری کرنے پر مبنی صلاحیت سے عاری ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ کفار کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان یا دار الحرب ( سرزمین کفر ) میں موجود مسلمان تاجر کی امان نا قابل تسلیم متصور ہوگی۔ ذی عقل کی صفت کا حامل مسلمان اپنی تدابیر کے ذریعے اہل کفر کو خوف زدہ رکھتا ہے اس لئے عقل و خر در کھنے والا مسلمان اہل کفر کی نظر میں محل خوف کا حامل ہوتا ہے جب کہ کفر کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان یا سرزمین کفر میں تنہا تا جر مسلمان اپنی بے بسی و بے کسی کے باعث حواس باختہ ہوتا ہے اس لئے مسلمان قیدی یا تاجر امان دینے کی اہمیت کا حامل نہیں ہوتا۔ صاحب قتال ہونا یاڈی عقل ہونے کا دارو مدار آزادانہ زندگی پر منحصر ہے۔ اگر اسے (مسلمان کو ) آزادانہ زندگی میسر نہیں تو صاحب قتال ہونے یا عقلمند ہونے کی صلاحیت باقی نہیں رہتی۔ لہذا آزادی ایسی صفت نہ ہونے کے بسبب انسان بنیادی طور پر امان کی مصلحت ( محل خوف کھو دیتا ہے۔ اس لئے ہر سہ صفات (اہل قال ذی عقل، آزادی) کا وجود اہل کفر کو امان دینے کیلئے مستلزم ہے۔ جب کہ کفار کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان اور مملکت کفریہ میں موجود تاجر امان کی مصلحت( محل خوف) سے خارج ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا مسلمان قیدی یا دار الحرب میں جانے والا تاجر کسی کافر کو یا دارالحرب کے تمام کفار کو امان دینے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ - اگر کفار کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان قیدی یا سرزمین کفر ( دار الحرب ) میں موجود تاجر کی امان کو قبول کر لیا جائے تو دارالحرب کے حوالے سے مجاہدین اسلام کی فتوحات میں رکاوٹ پیدا ہو جائے گی جو کہ نہ صرف اسلام، شعائر اسلام اور اہل اسلام کے حق میں نقصان دہ
It has also been said that a Muslim who is in the possession of the unbelievers and is their prisoner, or who is present among them for trade with a safe-conduct, his granting of aman to those warring unbelievers is not acceptable. Because both are under the control and possession of the unbelievers, so the unbelievers have no fear or danger from them. While aman is acceptable only from one from whom there is fear and danger. That is, the aman of one whom the unbelievers fear will be valid. Also by the proof that the unbelievers can force them to grant and write aman. Hence such aman will be outside the benefit of the Muslims. Also by the proof that if the aman given by a prisoner or trader were accepted, then whenever the Muslims become severe against the warring people, they would seize a Muslim prisoner or trader and force him to grant aman and thus escape. The result would be that the door of conquest over the unbelievers would be forever closed for the mujahideen. And a person who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb but does not migrate to dar al-Islam, his granting of aman is also not valid (because the unbelievers have no fear or danger from him, while the validity of aman is specific to one from whom the seeker of aman fears danger). It is clear that the slave who is given permission has two possibilities: either he is constrained, meaning he has no permission from his master to conduct any transaction or business; or he is authorized, meaning his master has given him permission for business and fighting. There is some difference in ruling between these two, which the author has explained in the chapter on worship. Explanation of the issue: A Muslim who goes to the unbelievers as a prisoner or with aman for trade, his granting of aman to the warring people is not permissible. Because the Muslim prisoner or trader is subjugated under the control of the unbelievers. Aman is specific to a place of fear, and that fear is not present with the people of disbelief. That is, the one from whom the people of disbelief fear, his aman is valid. Another proof is that the unbelievers will forcibly demand aman from the prisoner or trader. Thus the act of granting aman will be outside benefit. If the unbelievers capture a prisoner or trader, they will obtain release through the guise of aman from them. Then in that case, the door of conquest for the people of Islam does not open. The principle of validity of aman is that before granting aman, the hidden circumstances of strength and weakness should be considered. If the mujahideen of Islam present in dar al-Islam or the battlefield are strong at the time of offering aman and it is impossible for the unbelievers to cause harm, then granting aman is considered a correct step. Otherwise, the people of disbelief may cause harm by giving refuge. Therefore, situations based on internal weakness do not necessitate granting aman. Hence the principle of granting aman is to look at the internal conditions of dar al-Islam and the mujahideen of Islam. This makes clear that no Muslim deserves to grant aman to the unbelievers unless he is fully aware of the internal hidden conditions of dar al-Islam or the mujahideen engaged in battle with the people of disbelief. Since the Muslim prisoner confined in the custody of the unbelievers or the Muslim trader in the land of disbelief is unaware of the hidden conditions of dar al-Islam and the mujahideen, therefore the aman given by the prisoner or trader will be unacceptable. The Muslim prisoner or trader both are in the possession of the unbelievers. The unbelievers have the authority to use them as they wish. Lest they become harmful for the people of Islam under the guise of these prisoners or traders. Therefore, to remain safe from the harm of the unbelievers, it was deemed necessary to declare the aman of a Muslim confined in the custody of the unbelievers or a trader present in dar al-harb as unacceptable, so that the deceptions and cunning tricks of disbelief face failure and all Muslims remain safe from their evil and harm. 4. One of the pillars of aman is that the person granting aman be free. While a person confined in the custody of the unbelievers, although he is a Muslim and basically free, but having come into the possession of the unbelievers, he becomes completely constrained at the time. Because he is entirely at the mercy of the unbelievers. Therefore, considering the temporary captivity of the prisoner, he is not considered capable of granting aman. The same is the case of the Muslim trader who is in dar al-harb (the land of disbelief) due to trade needs and being far from the border of dar al-Islam, he is dependent on the people of disbelief. Hence the Muslim prisoner and the Muslim trader in dar al-harb, being helpless and subjugated opposite the unbelievers, do not possess the capability to grant aman to the people of Islam. 5. On the basis of benefit, aman is specific to a place of fear. That is, the unbelievers always fear a Muslim who is characterized by the qualities of being a warrior, intelligent, and free. Because the warrior not only remains armed but is always engaged in overpowering the unbelievers. Thus a Muslim possessing the quality of being a warrior causes the unbelievers to be intimidated, and the fear of the Muslim warrior remains upon them at all times. While the Muslim prisoner of the unbelievers cannot create even a particle of fear in the hearts of the people of disbelief. Because he lacks the ability to inspire fear. Therefore, the aman of a Muslim confined in the custody of the unbelievers or a Muslim trader present in dar al-harb (the land of disbelief) will be considered unacceptable. A Muslim possessing the quality of intelligence keeps the people of disbelief fearful through his strategies. Hence a Muslim with intellect and cunning is a place of fear in the eyes of the people of disbelief. While a Muslim confined in the custody of disbelief or a lone Muslim trader in the land of disbelief, due to his helplessness and loneliness, becomes agitated. Therefore, a Muslim prisoner or trader does not hold the importance of granting aman. Being a warrior or being intelligent depends on a free life. If a Muslim does not have a free life, then the capability of being a warrior or intelligent does not remain. Hence due to the absence of the quality of freedom, a person essentially loses the benefit of aman (place of fear). Therefore, the existence of all three qualities (warrior, intelligent, freedom) is necessary for granting aman to the people of disbelief. While a Muslim confined in the custody of the unbelievers and a trader present in the land of disbelief are outside the benefit of aman (place of fear). Hence a Muslim prisoner or a trader going to dar al-harb is not authorized to grant aman to any disbeliever or to all the disbelievers of dar al-harb. If the aman of a Muslim prisoner confined in the custody of the unbelievers or a trader present in the land of disbelief (dar al-harb) were accepted, then with respect to dar al-harb, there would be an obstacle in the conquests of the mujahideen of Islam, which is harmful not only for Islam, the symbols of Islam, and the people of Islam.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding the validity of aman (safe conduct) granted by a Muslim prisoner or merchant in dar al-harb. The author establishes that such aman is invalid and provides multiple rational proofs. The core principle is that aman is only valid from one who inspires fear in the enemy. A prisoner or merchant under enemy control does not inspire fear because they are in a position of weakness. The author also addresses the case of a Muslim who converts in dar al-harb but does not migrate, stating that his aman is also invalid for the same reason. The commentary emphasizes the importance of considering the strength and weakness of the Muslims when granting aman. It also notes that freedom is a necessary condition for the validity of aman, and a prisoner or dependent merchant lacks that freedom. The passage concludes by warning that accepting such aman would hinder Muslim conquests.

Key Terms
امان (aman): Safe conduct or guarantee of security granted to an enemy combatant, allowing them to enter Muslim territory without harm.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under the control of non-Muslims that is not bound by a peace treaty with Muslims.
قیدی (qaydi): A Muslim prisoner of war captured by the enemy and held in their custody.
محل خوف (mahall al-khawf): A place or person from whom one fears harm; it is a condition for aman that the granter be a source of fear to the enemy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the aman of a Muslim prisoner in dar al-harb considered invalid according to this passage?
A) Because prisoners are not Muslims.
B) Because the prisoner does not have the permission of the Muslim ruler.
C) Because the prisoner is under enemy control and does not inspire fear in the enemy.
D) Because aman can only be given by a free man, and prisoners are considered slaves.

Key Takeaway
Aman is only valid from a Muslim who is in a position of strength that inspires fear in the enemy; prisoners and merchants in dar al-harb lack this position, so their aman is invalid.

intermediate
8 min
The Invalidity of Aman from Captive or Dependent Muslims
Ruling statement on the invalidity of aman from captives and dependent traders

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid aman and explain why a Muslim prisoner or trader in dar al-harb cannot grant it.

Core Idea
Aman requires the granter to be free, capable of fighting, and independent — captives and dependent traders lack these.

Amān (safe conduct) is a critical tool in Islamic law for protecting life and property across conflict zones. However, not every Muslim is authorized to grant it. This passage clarifies that Muslims who themselves are under the control of the enemy—whether as prisoners or as vulnerable traders—cannot grant effective aman. The ruling is rooted in the purpose of aman: to instill fear in the enemy and thereby protect Muslims, a purpose that captives and dependent traders cannot fulfill.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a Muslim prisoner or trader in dar al-harb granting aman to a disbeliever. Ruling: invalid (impermissible).
The ruling is based on the granter's condition, not the recipient's.
2
List the prerequisites for valid aman
The text mentions three qualities: freedom, being a fighter (ṣāḥib qitāl), and intelligence (dhi ʿaql). These together create 'maḥall khawf' — the capacity to instill fear.
Freedom is described as a pillar (rukn) of aman.
3
Apply the prerequisites to the captive/trader
A prisoner, though essentially free, is under enemy control and thus effectively unfree. A trader in dar al-harb is dependent on the enemy. Both lack combat capability and the ability to instill fear.
Temporary helplessness negates the quality of 'ṣāḥib qitāl'.
4
Understand the rationale (maslahah)
Aman must serve the public interest by protecting Muslims. Accepting aman from a captive would allow enemy deception and hinder jihad and conquest.
Passage emphasizes preventing harm to the Muslim community and justice for all.
5
Extend the ruling to a new Muslim in dar al-harb
A harbī who converts to Islam in enemy territory is similarly dependent until he migrates to dar al-Islam. His aman is also invalid.
This extension is based on the same logic of dependency and lack of freedom.

دہ ثابت ہوں۔ چنانچہ کفار کے ضرر سے محفوظ رہتے کیلئے یہ امرضروری قرار پایا کہ کفار کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان یا دل الحرب میں موجود تاجر کی امان کو نا قابل قبول قرار دیا جائے تا کہ کفر کی فریب کاریوں اور عیارانہ چالوں کو ناکامی کا سامنا ہو اور تمام مسلمان ان کے شر اور نقصان سے محفوظ ہوسکیں ۔ ۴۔ امان کے ارکان میں سے ایک رکن یہ ہے کہ امان دینے والا شخص آزاد ہو جب کہ کفار کی قید میں محبوس آدمی اگر چہ مسلمان اور بنیادی طور پر آزاد ہوتا ہے لیکن کفار کے قبضہ میں آنے کے باعث وہ فی الوقت مجبور محض ہو جاتا ہے۔ بایں وجہ کہ وہ ( مسلمان قیدی ) ہمہ تن کفار کے رحم و کرم پر ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ قیدی کی وقتی اسارت (قید) کے پیش نظر اسے ( مسلمان قیدی کو امان دینے کے قابل نہیں سمجھا جاتا۔ یہی حال اس مسلمان تاجر کا ہے جو دار الحرب ( مملکت کفریہ ) میں تجارتی ضرورتوں اور دار الاسلام کی سرحد سے کوسوں دور ہونے کی وجہ ہے اہل کفر کامحتاج ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا مسلمان قیدی اور دار الحرب میں مسلمان تاجر کفار کے مد مقابل مجبور و مقہور ہونے کے باعث اہل اسلام کو امان دینے کی لیاقت نہیں رکھتا۔ ۵- از روی مصلحت امان محل خوف کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ یعنی کفار ہمیشہ ایسے مسلمان سے خائف ہوتے ہیں جو صاحب قتال وذی عقل اور آزادی پر مبنی صفات سے متصف ہو۔ کیونکہ اہل قبال نہ صرف ہمیشہ مسلح رہتا ہے بلکہ کفار کو سرنگوں کرنے کے عمل میں ہر وقت مصروف رہتا ہے۔ چنانچہ اہل قتال کی صفت کا حامل مسلمان کفار کی مرعوبیت کا باعث ہی نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ہر وقت ان (کفار ) پر مسلمان اہل قتال کا خوف بھی طاری رہتا ہے۔ جب کہ کفار کا قیدی (مسلمان) اہل کفر کے دلوں میں ذرہ بھر خوف طاری نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ وہ (مسلمان قید یا دار الحرب میں موجود تا جر ) خوف طاری کرنے پر مبنی صلاحیت سے عاری ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ کفار کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان یا دار الحرب ( سرزمین کفر ) میں موجود مسلمان تاجر کی امان نا قابل تسلیم متصور ہوگی۔ ذی عقل کی صفت کا حامل مسلمان اپنی تدابیر کے ذریعے اہل کفر کو خوف زدہ رکھتا ہے اس لئے عقل و خر در کھنے والا مسلمان اہل کفر کی نظر میں محل خوف کا حامل ہوتا ہے جب کہ کفر کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان یا سرزمین کفر میں تنہا تا جر مسلمان اپنی بے بسی و بے کسی کے باعث حواس باختہ ہوتا ہے اس لئے مسلمان قیدی یا تاجر امان دینے کی اہمیت کا حامل نہیں ہوتا۔ صاحب قتال ہونا یاڈی عقل ہونے کا دارو مدار آزادانہ زندگی پر منحصر ہے۔ اگر اسے (مسلمان کو ) آزادانہ زندگی میسر نہیں تو صاحب قتال ہونے یا عقلمند ہونے کی صلاحیت باقی نہیں رہتی۔ لہذا آزادی ایسی صفت نہ ہونے کے بسبب انسان بنیادی طور پر امان کی مصلحت ( محل خوف کھو دیتا ہے۔ اس لئے ہر سہ صفات (اہل قال ذی عقل، آزادی) کا وجود اہل کفر کو امان دینے کیلئے مستلزم ہے۔ جب کہ کفار کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان اور مملکت کفریہ میں موجود تاجر امان کی مصلحت( محل خوف) سے خارج ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا مسلمان قیدی یا دار الحرب میں جانے والا تاجر کسی کافر کو یا دارالحرب کے تمام کفار کو امان دینے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ - اگر کفار کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان قیدی یا سرزمین کفر ( دار الحرب ) میں موجود تاجر کی امان کو قبول کر لیا جائے تو دارالحرب کے حوالے سے مجاہدین اسلام کی فتوحات میں رکاوٹ پیدا ہو جائے گی جو کہ نہ صرف اسلام، شعائر اسلام اور اہل اسلام کے حق میں نقصان دہ امر ہے بلکہ اسلام دشمن اور شر پسند عناصر کے جوروستم میں پسنے والی انسانیت کا بھی قلع قمع ہو جائے گا۔ چنانچہ کفار کی قید میں ایک یا چند مسلمان قیدیوں یا دار الحر میں چند تا جبران کی خاطر مظلوم عوام ( مسلمان و کافر) کے مشترکہ مفادات کو سبو تا ثر کر نا حق و انصاف کے خلاف ہے۔ لہذا حق و انصاف کے تقاضوں کو پورا کرنے اور اس کے پس منظر میں مجاہدین اسلام کیلئے فتوحات کا دروازہ کھلا رکھنے کیلئے ضروری ہے کہ کفار کے قبضے میں ایک یا چند مسلمان قیدیوں یا دار الحرب میں موجود چند تاجروں کی امان کو عدم جواز کا درجہ دیا جائے ۔ ۷۔ مملکت کفریہ میں اسلام لانے والے حربی کی امان کو صیح و جائز متصور نہ کیا جائے گا تاوقتیکہ وہ ( حربی ) دارالاسلام کی طرف ہجرت نہ کر لے۔ کیونکہ دارالحرب میں اسلام قبول کرنے والے حربی کی حیثیت بھی وہی ہوگی جو کفار کی قید میں محبوس مسلمان قیدی یا دار الحرب میں موجود تا جر کی ہے۔
Whether a Muslim is a prisoner or a trader, both are in the possession of the disbelievers. The disbelievers are authorized to use them (the Muslim prisoner/trader) as they wish, lest they (the prisoner/trader) become harmful to the people of Islam under their guise. Therefore, to remain safe from the harm of the disbelievers, it was deemed necessary that the aman of a Muslim imprisoned by the disbelievers or a trader present in dar al-harb be considered unacceptable, so that the deceptions and cunning tricks of disbelief face failure and all Muslims can be safe from their evil and harm. 4. Among the pillars of aman is that the person granting aman be free. While a person imprisoned by the disbelievers is essentially a free Muslim, due to falling into the possession of the disbelievers he becomes completely helpless at the moment. Because the Muslim prisoner is entirely at the mercy of the disbelievers. Considering the prisoner's temporary captivity, he is not considered qualified to grant aman. The same applies to a Muslim trader in dar al-harb (the land of disbelief) who, due to commercial needs and being miles away from the border of dar al-Islam, is dependent on the people of disbelief. Therefore, a Muslim prisoner and a Muslim trader in dar al-harb, being helpless and oppressed vis-à-vis the disbelievers, are not qualified to grant aman to the people of Islam. 5. As a matter of public interest (maslahah), aman is specific to a place of fear. That is, the disbelievers are always afraid of a Muslim who possesses the qualities of being a fighter (sahib qital), intelligent (dhi 'aql), and free. Because a person of combat is not only always armed but also constantly engaged in the process of subduing the disbelievers. Thus, a Muslim possessing the quality of being a fighter not only causes the disbelievers to be intimidated but also the fear of a Muslim fighter is always upon them. Whereas a Muslim prisoner cannot instill an iota of fear in the hearts of the disbelievers. Because he lacks the capacity to create fear. Therefore, the aman of a Muslim imprisoned by the disbelievers or a Muslim trader present in the land of disbelief will be deemed unacceptable. A Muslim possessing the quality of intelligence keeps the disbelievers fearful through his strategies, so an intelligent Muslim is considered a source of fear in the eyes of the disbelievers. In contrast, a Muslim imprisoned in disbelief or a lone trader in the land of disbelief is frantic due to his helplessness and destitution, so a Muslim prisoner or trader does not hold the importance of granting aman. Being a fighter or being intelligent depends on a free life. If he does not have a free life, then the ability to be a fighter or intelligent does not remain. Therefore, due to the absence of the quality of freedom, a person essentially loses the maslahah of aman (the place of fear). Thus, the existence of all three qualities (fighter, intelligent, freedom) is necessary for granting aman to the disbelievers. Whereas a Muslim imprisoned by the disbelievers and a trader present in the land of disbelief are outside the maslahah of aman (place of fear). Therefore, a Muslim prisoner or a trader going to dar al-harb is not authorized to grant aman to any disbeliever or to all the disbelievers of dar al-harb. - If the aman of a Muslim prisoner imprisoned by the disbelievers or a trader present in the land of disbelief is accepted, then obstacles will arise in the conquests of the Muslim mujahideen regarding dar al-harb, which is not only harmful to Islam, its symbols, and the people of Islam, but will also eliminate the humanity suffering under the tyranny of the enemies of Islam and evil elements. Therefore, sacrificing the common interests of the oppressed masses (Muslims and disbelievers) for the sake of one or several Muslim prisoners in the captivity of the disbelievers or a few traders in dar al-harb is against justice and fairness. Hence, to fulfill the demands of justice and fairness and to keep the door of conquest open for the Muslim mujahideen in this context, it is necessary that the aman of one or several Muslim prisoners in the possession of the disbelievers or a few traders present in dar al-harb be deemed impermissible. 7. The aman of a harbi who accepts Islam in the land of disbelief will not be considered valid and permissible until he migrates to dar al-Islam. Because the status of a harbi who accepts Islam in dar al-harb is the same as that of a Muslim prisoner imprisoned by the disbelievers or a trader present in dar al-harb.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining why a Muslim prisoner or trader in enemy territory cannot grant aman (safe conduct) to disbelievers. The author establishes that aman is only valid from a free Muslim who is capable of fighting (sahib qital) and intelligent, because the purpose of aman is to create fear in the disbelievers, thereby protecting Muslims. A prisoner or trader is under the control of the disbelievers, so they cannot instill that fear. The reasoning is based on public interest (maslahah) and the need to prevent harm to the Muslim community. The passage also extends this ruling to a harbi who converts to Islam while still in dar al-harb; his aman is invalid until he migrates to dar al-Islam. The author emphasizes that accepting such aman would obstruct the jihad and conquests of the Muslim mujahideen, leading to harm for both Muslims and oppressed humanity. The key principle is that aman must come from a position of strength and freedom, not from captivity or dependency.

Key Terms
امان (amān): A contract of safe conduct granted to a non-Muslim enemy, guaranteeing security of life and property.
صاحب قتال (ṣāḥib qitāl): A person who is capable and authorized to engage in combat against the enemy.
محل خوف (maḥall khawf): The quality that instills fear in the enemy; a prerequisite for the validity of aman according to this text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the aman of a Muslim trader in dar al-harb invalid?
A) Because he is not physically present in dar al-Islam.
B) Because he is dependent on the disbelievers and lacks effective freedom and combat capability.
C) Because he is not a scholar of Islam.
D) Because he did not receive permission from the Muslim ruler.

Key Takeaway
Aman is only valid when granted by a free Muslim combatant who can instill fear in the enemy; captives and dependent traders cannot grant it.

intermediate
8 min
Slave's Aman: Abu Hanifa vs. Shaybani
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of a restricted slave's aman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on a restricted slave's aman and distinguish the legal proofs of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Aman requires capacity to instill fear; a fighting-restricted slave lacks it.

Aman (safe conduct) is a critical tool in Islamic law of war. Who can grant it? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether a restricted slave (abd mahjur) can grant aman. Abu Hanifa says no without fighting permission; Muhammad says yes. The disagreement rests on the hadith of the Prophet and the nature of aman as a fear-based instrument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling per each Imam
State the ruling for a restricted slave granting aman: Abu Hanifa says invalid unless master permits fighting; Muhammad says valid absolutely.
Remember that 'mahjur' means restricted from fighting and transactions.
2
Analyze Muhammad's proof: hadith and analogy
Muhammad cites the hadith 'Aman of a slave is aman' and argues by analogy: the slave is a believer capable of resistance, so his aman is valid like that of a free fighter.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Musa al-Ash'ari; some Hanafis consider it weak.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof: lack of capacity to instill fear
Abu Hanifa argues that a restricted slave cannot fight, so disbelievers do not fear him; thus aman misses its purpose. Also, the slave's action may harm his master.
Abu Hanifa emphasizes that aman must meet its mahall (proper context).
4
Note Abu Yusuf's dual narration and cross-madhhab agreement
Abu Yusuf has two narrations, one with each. Al-Shafi'i agrees with Muhammad, showing the dispute is not merely intra-Hanafi.
This affects the weight of the respective proofs.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position and practical consequence
The relied-upon Hanafi position is Abu Hanifa's: a restricted slave cannot grant aman without fighting permission. The practical difference: if such a slave grants aman, it is invalid and must be rejected.
The tarjih is based on stronger analogy and preservation of the master's rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَمَانُ الْعَبْدِ الْمَحْجُورٍ عِندَأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَأْذَنَ لَهُ مَوْلَاهُ فِي الْقِتَالِ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَصِحُ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الشَّافِعِي وَ أَبُو يُوْسُفَ مَعَهُ فِي رِوَايَةٍ وَمَعَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةً فِي رِوَايَةٍ لِمُحَمَّدٍ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَمَانُ الْعَبْدِ أَمَانَ رَوَاهُ أَبُو مُوسَى الْأَشْعَرِى وَلانَّهُ مُؤْمِنٌ مُمْتَنِعُ فَيَصِحُ أَمَانَهُ اِعْتِبَارًا بِالْمَادُونِ لَهُ فِي الْقِتَالِ وَبِالْمُؤيَّدِمِنَ الْأَمَانِ وَالْإِيْمَانُ لكَوْنِهِ شَرُطًا لِلْعِبَادَةِ وَالْجِهَادُ عِبَادَةَ وَالاِمْتِنَاعُ لِتَحَقِّقِ إِزَالَةِ الْخَوفِ بِهِ وَ النَّاثِير إِعْزَازُ الدِّيْنِ وَإِقَامَةُ الْمَصْلَحَةِ فِى حَقِّ جَمَاعَةِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ إِذْ الْكَلَامُ فِي مِثْلِ هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ وَإِنَّمَا لَا يَمْلِكُ الْمُسَابَقَةِ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنْ تَعْطِيلِ مَنَافِع الْمَوْلى وَلَا تَعْطِيْلَ فِي مُجَرِدِ الْقَولِ وَالأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ مَحْجُورٌ عَنِ الْقِتَالِ فَلَا يَصِحُ أَمَانُهُ لأَنَّهُمْ لاَ يَخَافُونَهُ فَلَمْ يُلاقِ الْأَمَانُ مَحَلَّهُ بِخِلَافِ الْمَادُون لَهُ فِي الْقِتَالِ لِأَنَّ الْحَوْفَ مِنْهُ مُتَحَقَّقُ وَلِأَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا لَا يَمْلِكُ الْمُسَابَقَةَ لِمَا أَنَّهُ تَـ تَصَرُّفَ فِى حَقِّ الْمَوِلِى عَلى وَجْهِ لَا يَعْرُى عَنِ احْتِمَالِ الضَّرَرِ فِى حَقِ، وَالْأَمَانُ تَوحُ قِتَالِ وَفِيهِ مَا ذَكَرْنَاهُ لأَنَّهُ قَدْيُخْطِئُ بَلْ هُوَ الظَّاهِرُ وَ فِيهِ سَبَابِ الْاِسْتِغْنَامِ بِخِلَافِ الْمَادُونِ لأَنَّهُ رَضِيَ بِهِ وَالْخَطَاءَ نَادِرُ لِمُبَاشَرَتِهِ الْقِتَالَ وَ بِخِلَافِ الْمُؤيَّدِ لِأَنَّهُ خَلَفَ عَنِ الْإِسْلَامِ فَهُوَ بِمَنزِلَةِ الدَّعْوَةِ إِلَيْهِ وَلِأَنَّهُ مُقَابِلُ بِالْجِزْيَةِ وَلِأَنَّهُ مَفْرُوضُ ثمَّ ذَالِكَ وَإِسْقَ الفَرضِ نَفعُ فَافترقا
And the aman of a restricted slave is not valid according to Abu Hanifa unless his master permits him to fight. And Muhammad said: it is valid, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i. And Abu Yusuf is with him (Muhammad) in one narration, and with Abu Hanifa in another narration. For Muhammad (al-Shaybani), his (the Prophet's) statement, peace be upon him: 'The aman of a slave is aman,' narrated by Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. And because he is a believer who is capable of resistance/self-defense, so his aman is valid, by analogy (i'tibar) with one who is less than him in fighting, and with the mu'ayyad (the one given authority/?) of aman. And faith is a condition for worship, and jihad is worship. And resistance/self-defense achieves the removal of fear through it. And the consideration (al-nazr) is the elevation of the religion and the establishment of maslahah with regard to the community of Muslims, for the discussion is in such a situation. And indeed he does not own the musabaqah (?) because of what it entails in terms of disrupting the benefits of the master, and there is no disruption in mere speech. And Abu Hanifa's (argument is) that he (the slave) is restricted from fighting, so his aman is not valid, because they (the disbelievers) do not fear him, so the aman does not meet its proper place (mahall). Unlike one who is less than him in fighting, because fear from him is realized. And because he does not own the musabaqah because it is a disposal concerning the master in a way that is not free from the possibility of harm with respect to him. And aman is a matter of fighting, and in it is what we mentioned, because he might err, rather it is apparent, and in it is the cause of plunder (istighnam). Unlike one who is less, because he is pleased with it, and error is rare due to his direct engagement in fighting. And unlike the mu'ayyad, because he is a successor of Islam, so he is like a call to it. And because he is faced with jizyah. And because that (jizyah) is fard, and dropping a fard is a benefit, so they differ.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a restricted slave (abd mahjur) can grant aman. Abu Hanifa holds that such a slave cannot grant aman unless his master has permitted him to fight. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that it is valid, and this is also the view of al-Shafi'i. Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one with Muhammad and one with Abu Hanifa. Muhammad's proof is the hadith 'Aman of a slave is aman' (though not widely authenticated) and an analogy: the slave is a believer capable of self-defense, so his aman is valid, just like a free fighter. He also argues that faith is a condition for worship like jihad, and the slave's aman serves the maslahah of the Muslim community. Abu Hanifa's argument is that the slave is restricted from fighting, so the disbelievers do not fear him, and thus the aman does not achieve its purpose. He also notes that the slave's action might cause harm to the master and lead to plunder. The passage concludes by distinguishing the slave from a free fighter (madun) and a mu'ayyad (probably a dhimmi or someone under treaty), because the latter are authorized or have a different legal basis.

Key Terms
المحجور (al-maḥjūr): A slave who is restricted by his master from engaging in financial transactions and fighting.
أمان العبد (amān al-ʿabd): The aman (safe conduct) granted by a slave.
الْمُؤيَّد (al-muʾayyad): A person who is supported or given authority, possibly a dhimmi or a Muslim under treaty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, a restricted slave can only grant valid aman if:
A) The slave is also a free man.
B) The slave's master has permitted him to fight.
C) The enemy is unaware of the slave's status.
D) The slave is literate.

Key Takeaway
A restricted slave's aman is invalid in the Hanafi school unless the master has permitted fighting, because the slave cannot instill the necessary fear.

Aman by a Slave in Jihad: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Historical incident and legal analysis of a slave's aman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of aman by a slave who is not permitted to fight, identify the proofs of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the preferred view (mufta bihi) in a battlefield scenario.

Core Idea
A slave's aman is valid if he is a believer and can inspire fear; the Sahibayn's view prevails over Abu Hanifa's.

This passage examines a classical dispute within the Hanafi school concerning the validity of aman (safe conduct) granted by a slave during jihad. The issue arises from a historical incident involving the Companions and the Caliph Umar (RA), whose verdict provides a key proof. The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, turns on whether the slave's permission to fight matters, or whether the enemy's perception of fear is sufficient. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi methodology of weighing proofs (dalil) and considering public interest (maslaha) in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its context
The act is granting aman by a slave in the battlefield. The context is jihad, and the slave may be either permitted (ma'dhun) or not permitted (majbur) to fight by his master.
Aman is a contract of safe conduct. The slave's status is key.
2
State the intra-Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa says aman is invalid if the slave is not permitted; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) say it is valid even then.
Both sides agree on validity when the slave is permitted.
3
Examine the proofs of each side
Abu Hanifa argues that without the ability to fight, the enemy has no fear, so aman is futile. The Sahibayn rely on Umar's verdict, qiyas to a permitted slave and to dhimma, and the enemy's indistinguishable fear.
The dalil_block in this lesson records the key proof from Umar (RA).
4
Analyze the tahamul (objection and rebuttal)
Ibn al-Humam objects to Abu Hanifa's premise: the enemy cannot distinguish between permitted and non-permitted slaves, so fear exists in all cases.
This objection supports the Sahibayn's view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi practice adopts the Sahibayn's view, supported by the story of Umar and the maslaha of protecting Muslim interests.
The mufta bihi is the operative ruling for fatwa.

بجالا نا عين نفع ہے۔ اس طرح كا فر كو ذمی بننے كا عہد نامہ دينے اور لڑائی كے موقع میں امان دينے كے درميان واضح فرق ہے۔
We besieged a city of theirs for a month. Finally one morning we thought we would conquer it, so we withdrew from fighting. Coincidentally, our slave remained there. The infidels sought aman from him, and he wrote a document of aman and threw it to them with an arrow. Having received it, they laid down their arms, put on their clothes, and came out to us. We asked them what their situation was. They replied that you have given us aman, and they presented the document. After reading it, we said this is from a slave who does not have the authority to grant aman. They said we do not distinguish between your free men and slaves; that is why we came to you after receiving the aman. Then we wrote the whole incident to Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). He replied: A Muslim slave is among the Muslims, and his aman is also the aman of the Muslims. Ibn Abi Shaybah also narrated this. And by this proof, the aman of a slave is valid because that slave is a believer and possesses power. Therefore, his aman will be valid, just as the aman of a slave who is permitted to fight is valid, and just as if a slave writes a covenant for an infidel to live as a dhimmi in his land, which is accepted. Here we have stipulated the condition of faith, i.e., the one granting aman must be a believer, because faith is a condition for any act of worship, and jihad is an act of worship. Similarly, we have stipulated the second condition of possessing power, because by it the removal of fear from others becomes certain. And the compelled slave (majbur) is analogized to the permitted slave (ma'dhun) because in both granting aman, the honor of the religion and the consideration of the Muslims' interest are equal. This detail applies when the slave's granting of aman is in accordance with the Muslims' interest. The power of a compelled slave to fight is not considered, because if he were independent and could do as he pleases, he would not be able to perform his obligatory service to his master; he only has the right to grant aman in one saying because his (master's) heavy service is not diminished. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that when this slave has no right to fight, his aman will not be valid because in such a case the infidels have no fear of him. So his aman would be untimely and useless, unlike the slave who is permitted to fight, because the presence of fear from him is certain. (Ibn al-Humam objected: The infidels do not distinguish which slave is permitted and which is compelled, so they fear every slave; rather, fear is certainly present. Another proof is that a common slave has no leisure to kill because he is fully occupied in his master's service, so he would cause harm by doing any other work, or the possibility of harm cannot be ruled out. His granting aman is also a type of fighting, and his engagement in fighting is a total loss for his master, because perhaps the slave may commit an error or mistake; rather, this possibility is clear. Thus, in the future, his master will not get any share of the spoils, and the door of spoils will be closed for him, unlike the permitted slave, because his master is mentally prepared for everything, and such a slave rarely makes a mistake since he has already participated in fighting. And this matter is not like giving a covenant to a dhimmi; i.e., if a compelled slave writes a covenant for an infidel to become a dhimmi and live in his land, it will be accepted because he has permission for that, because the infidel becoming a dhimmi is equivalent to his conversion from disbelief to Islam. Thus, giving a covenant to an infidel is like inviting him to Islam; along with that, jizya is also collected from this dhimmi. In this way, every kind of benefit is obtained. Also, because when an infidel requests to become a dhimmi, accepting it becomes obligatory (fard), and fulfilling a fard is pure benefit. Thus, there is a clear difference between giving a covenant to an infidel to become a dhimmi and granting aman in the battlefield.)
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of aman (safe conduct) given by a slave during jihad. The discussion begins with a historical incident: during a siege, a slave remaining behind wrote an aman document and threw it to the enemy. When the companions questioned the validity, Umar (RA) affirmed that a Muslim slave's aman is like that of a Muslim. This ruling establishes that a slave's aman is valid if he is a believer (mumin) and possesses power (sahib quwwa) to inspire fear in the enemy. The text then introduces the condition of being 'permitted to fight' (ma'dhun). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if a slave is not permitted to fight (majbur), his aman is invalid because the enemy will not fear him, making the aman futile. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the enemy does not distinguish between permitted and non-permitted slaves; they fear all slaves equally, so the aman is valid. They analogize to a slave who gives a dhimma covenant, which is accepted. The text also mentions Ibn al-Humam's objection to Abu Hanifa, supporting the Sahibayn. The preferred view (mufta bihi) in later Hanafi practice is the validity of the aman, based on the story of Umar and maslaha (public interest). The key takeaway: a slave can give valid aman if he is a believer and capable of instilling fear, regardless of his master's permission in the battlefield context.

Key Terms
امان (aman): A contract of safe conduct granted to an enemy combatant, guaranteeing protection of life and property.
غلام (ghulam): A male slave, owned by a master. In this context, a slave who may or may not be permitted to fight.
ماذون (ma'dhun): A slave who has been granted permission by his master to engage in trade or, in this context, to participate in jihad and fighting.
مجبور (majbur): A slave who is not permitted by his master to fight or engage in activities beyond his basic service obligation.
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of an Islamic state, paying jizya in exchange for security.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when a slave who is not permitted to fight grants aman to the enemy?
A) Invalid
B) Valid
C) Valid only if the master consents
D) Invalid unless the slave is free

Key Takeaway
A slave's aman is valid in the Hanafi school if he inspires fear, irrespective of his master's permission, due to the Sahibayn's position.

The Validity of Aman Granted by a Minor
Ruling on aman by a minor with and without understanding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on aman granted by a minor in three distinct cases and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
A minor's aman is valid if he understands and is permitted to fight; otherwise, disagreement exists.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary addresses the complex question of whether a minor child can grant aman (safe conduct) to non-Muslims. The ruling hinges on the child's level of understanding ('aql) and whether he is authorized to participate in combat. We will explore the three scenarios presented and the differing opinions within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage distinguishes a minor who does not understand, one who understands but is prohibited from fighting, and one who is permitted to fight.
The key factor is the minor's 'aql (understanding) and permission to fight.
2
State the ruling for each
For the first scenario, the aman is invalid by consensus. For the third, it is valid by consensus. For the second, there is ikhtilaf.
The hadith of raf' al-qalam is cited but interpreted differently.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa says invalid; Imam Muhammad and others say valid. Examine the proofs for each.
The disagreement is based on whether the minor is considered ahl al-aman.
4
Examine the role of the hadith
The hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' is used to argue invalidity, but the Hanafi response limits its scope to accountability for sin, not validity of beneficial actions.
This is a key usul distinction between usul and furu'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative position for fatwa is that the aman is valid if the minor understands, even if not permitted to fight, following Imam Muhammad.
This view is preferred due to maslaha (public benefit).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صبي لَا يَعْقِلُ کی امان کا حکم
وَ لَوْ أمَنَ الصَّبِيُّ وَهُوَ لَا يَعْقِلُ لَا يَصِحُ كَالْمَجْنُونِ وَإِنْ كَانَ يَعْقِلْ وَهُوَ مَحْجُورٌ عَنِ الْقِتَالِ فَعَلَى الْخِلَافِ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَا ذُونَا لَهُ فِي الْقِتَالِ فَالْأَصْحُ أَنَّهُ يَصِحَ بِالْإِتِفَاقِ
ترجمہ اور اگر ایسے نابالغ نے امان دی ہو جو ابھی تک اسلام کے مفہوم کو نہیں سمجھتا ہو تو اس کی امان مجنوں کے امان کے مانند صحیح نہیں ہے اور اگر وہ نابالغ اسلامہ مفہوم بجھتا بھی ہوا سے قتال کرنے کی اجازت نہیں دی گئی ہو تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کی بھی امان صحیح نہیں ہے لیکن امام محمد اور باقی آئمہ کے نزدیک صحیح ہے اور اگر اسے قتال کی بھی اجازت مل چکی ہو تو قول اصبح یہ ہے کہ تمام آئمہ کے نزدیک بالا اتفاق صحیح ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہےکہ اگر نا سمجھ بچے نے کسی کا فریا کفار کے گروہ کو امان ( پناہ دی۔ تو جمہور علماء کے نزدیک اسلام کی سمجھ نہ رکھنے والے بچے کی امان صحیح نہیں ہے۔
ا۔ کیونکہ نابالغ بچہ امان پر بنی حکم حرمت قتال ، خطاب تحریم کے اعتبار سے اہل امان میں شمار نہیں ہوتا۔ ۲ اہل اسلام کے ضعف اور اہل کفر کی قوت پر مشتمل مخفی حالت سے آگاہی کا تعلق تفکر وتد برپرمبنی ہوتا ہے۔ جب کہ نابالغ و بے شعور بچہ کھیل کود کی طرف رغبت رکھتا ہے۔ لہذا نابالغ بچہ جہاں اہل ایمان نہیں ہوتا وہاں اہل امان ( پناہ) بھی متصور نہیں ہوتا۔ بقول امام شافعی رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام کا ارشاد ہے کہ تین آدمی مرفوع القلم ہیں۔۱۔ نابالغ بچہ ۲۔ دیوانہ ۔۳۔ نائم ( نیند کرنے والا ) گوکہ نابالغ بچہ کا عقلی اصول کے حوالے سے مرفوع القلم ہونا ممنوع ہے۔ لیکن فروعات شریعہ کے ضمن میں اسے ( نابالغ بچے کو ) مرفوع القلم (احکام شریعہ کا مکلف نہ ہونا ) متصور کیا جائے گا۔
The ruling on the aman of a minor who does not understand: If a minor grants aman while he does not understand, it is not valid, like a madman. And if he understands but is prohibited from fighting, then it is subject to ikhtilaf. And if he is permitted to fight, the most correct (asah) view is that it is valid by agreement. Translation: And if a minor who does not yet understand the concept of Islam gives aman, his aman is invalid like that of a madman. And if the minor understands the concept of Islam but has not been given permission to fight, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, his aman is invalid, but according to Imam Muhammad and the other imams, it is valid. And if he has been given permission to fight, the most correct view is that it is valid by consensus. Explanation: If a child who does not understand gives aman to a group of infidels, then according to the majority of scholars, the aman of a child who does not understand Islam is invalid. Because: 1. A minor child is not considered among the people eligible for aman based on the ruling of the prohibition of fighting and the address of prohibition. 2. Awareness of the hidden state involving the weakness of Muslims and the strength of infidels requires reflection and deliberation, while a minor and senseless child inclines towards play. Therefore, just as a minor child is not considered a believer, he is also not considered eligible for aman (protection). According to Imam Shafi'i, the Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him) said: Three people are not accountable: 1. A minor child, 2. A madman, 3. A sleeping person. Although in principle a minor child being not accountable is prohibited in terms of rational principles, in the furu' (branches) of shariah, he is considered not accountable (not obligated by legal rulings).
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on aman (safe conduct) given by a minor (sabi). It distinguishes three scenarios. First, a minor who lacks understanding ('aql) is like a madman; his aman is invalid by consensus. Second, a minor who understands but is prohibited from fighting (mahjur an al-qital) — here, Abu Hanifa rules the aman invalid, while Imam Muhammad and other imams rule it valid. The basis for the majority view is that the child, lacking full accountability (raf' al-qalam), is not a reliable grantor of aman. However, the counter-argument is that the child, if he understands, can recognize the benefit to Muslims. Third, if the minor is permitted to fight (ma'dhun), the most correct view (asah) is that the aman is valid by agreement (bil-ittifaq). The text then provides an explanation: the child who does not understand is not considered ahl al-aman because he lacks the capacity to appreciate the strategic considerations. The hadith 'three people are not accountable' (marfu' al-qalam) is cited from Imam Shafi'i as evidence for invalidity, but the Hanafi response clarifies that this hadith applies to accountability for sins, not necessarily to validity of actions like aman. In furu' matters, such as aman, the child's action may still be valid if it benefits the Muslims. The key takeaway: a minor's aman is most likely valid if he is permitted to fight; if not permitted, there is disagreement, but the later preference tends towards validity (Sahibayn's view).

Key Terms
صبي (sabi): A minor child who has not reached puberty.
يعقل (ya'qil): To possess understanding and reasoning, specifically the ability to comprehend the meaning of Islam and the implications of aman.
مجنون (majnun): An insane person who lacks reason entirely.
مرفوع القلم (marfu' al-qalam): A person from whom the pen of responsibility is lifted, i.e., not subject to divine commands or punishments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view (al-asah) in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the aman of a minor who understands and is permitted to fight?
A) Invalid by consensus
B) Valid by consensus
C) Valid according to Abu Hanifa only
D) Invalid according to Imam Muhammad

Key Takeaway
The validity of a minor's aman depends on his understanding and permission to fight, with the operative position favoring validity for understanding minors even if not permitted.

Validity of Amān by a Minor: Conditions and Scholarly Disputes
Inter-madhhab dispute on minor's amān

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a minor's amān to be valid and explain the Hanafi ruling on the disputed case.

Core Idea
A minor's amān is invalid unless he has understanding of Islam and is permitted to fight.

The general rule is that amān requires intellect and awareness of Muslims' strategic interests, which minors and the insane lack. However, a dispute arises when the minor is near puberty and understands Islam. This lesson dissects the Hanafi position and the scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
Recognize that the source establishes amān as a disposition requiring intellect and consciousness, thus excluding minors and the insane by default.
The principle is that amān depends on knowledge of Muslims' hidden conditions.
2
Isolate the Contested Case
Find the specific scenario: a minor who is near puberty and has understanding of Islam. Note that this case generates disagreement among fuqahā'.
Imam Muhammad holds it valid; the majority Hanafis reject it.
3
Examine the Opposing Proof
State Imam Muhammad's dalil: amān eligibility is based on faith eligibility, and the minor with understanding qualifies as a person of faith.
Also note that Malik and Ahmad in one view support this.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response and Consensus
Understand the majority's rebuttal: the minor lacks awareness of Muslims' secret conditions. Then see that if the minor is permitted to fight (and thus has that awareness), all schools agree on validity.
The relied-upon position is the consensus when the minor is permitted to fight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير
اسلامی احکامات پر مبنی عملی تصرفات کی اہلیت کے لئے عقل و شعور کا وجود لازمی ہے۔ امان دینا ایک شرعی تصرف ہے جو عقل و شعور کا مقتضی ہے اور صبی (عقل و شعور سے عاری بچہ) میں خرد (عقل) نام کی چیز نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اگر منتقل ہوتی بھی ہے تو وہ کھیل کود کی طرف راغب ہونے کی وجہ سے کا اعادم متصور ہوتی ہے۔ جب کہ امان دینے کے لئے تدبر و تفکر کا تحقق (ثبوت) لازمی امر ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ غیر ذی عقل و غیر ذی شعور شخص (خواہ نابالغ بچہ ہو یا بالغ دیوانہ) کسی کافر کو امان دینے کا مجاز نہیں۔ کیونکہ شریق تعرف کے لئے عقل و شعور مشروط ہے۔ 
امان کی شرائط میں سے ایک شرط بلاغت کی عدم موجودگی میں امان کا حق نا ممکن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ نا بالغ بچے میں حرمت قتال اور تحریم خطاب موجود نہیں۔
نابالغ بچے کی امان میں فقہاء کی اختلافی صورت: اگر بچہ بلوغت کے قریب ہے اور اسلام کی سمجھ بوجھ رکھتا ہے تو امام محمد کے نزدیک ایسے بچے کو یہ استحقاق حاصل ہے کہ وہ کسی کافر کو امان دے۔ بایں دلیل کہ امان کی اہلیت ایمان کی اہلیت پر مبنی ہے اور جو نا بالغ بچہ اسلام کی سمجھ بوجھ رکھتا ہے وہ اہل ایمان کے زمرے میں آتا ہے۔ البداوہ (نابالغ بچہ) بالغ آدمی کی طرح امان دینے کا مجاز ہوگا۔
امام مالک، امام احمد کی رائے بھی ایک قول کے مطابق امام محمد کے موقف کی تائید میں ہے اور ایک روایت کے مطابق امام شافعی، احمد، امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول کی تائید کرتے ہیں۔ جب کہ جمہور علماء (اصحاب احناف) کا استدلال یہ ہے کہ نابالغ بچہ امان کے علم کے اعتبار سے اہل امان میں سے نہیں کیونکہ امان کے جواز کے لئے مسلمانوں کی خفیہ حالات سے واقف اور غور و فکر رکھنے کی صلاحیت لازمی امر ہے جو کہ اس (نابالغ بچے) میں موجود نہیں لہذا الحناف کی رائے یہی ہے کہ نابالغ بچہ حکم امان کے پیش نظر امان دینے کا مجاز نہیں۔ بشرطیکہ وہ اسلام کی سمجھ بوجھ رکھنے والا نابالغ بچہ قتال میں ممنوع ہو۔ چنانچہ اس (نا بالغ) بچے کی امان بھی عبد مجور (قتال میں ممنوع غلام) جیسی ہوگی۔
فقہاء کی متفقہ صورت: اگر بچہ قتال میں اجازت یافتہ ہے تو مسلمانوں کی خفیہ حالت (ضعف وقوت) سے واقفیت رکھنے اور اسلام کی سمجھ بوجھ کا حامل ہونے کی بناء پر تمام فقہاء (خصوصا فقہائے احناف) کے نزدیک متفقہ طور پر اس (قتال میں اجازت یافتہ بچے) کی امان صحیح ہوگی۔ بقول صاحب ہدایہ یا قدوری اصح قول یہی ہے۔
Book of Siyar. For eligibility of practical dispositions based on Islamic rulings, intellect and consciousness are necessary. Giving amān is a shar‘ī disposition that requires intellect and consciousness, and a minor (a child devoid of intellect and consciousness) does not possess anything called intellect. Even if it transfers, due to inclination towards play, its non-existence is imagined. While for giving amān, certainty of deliberation and reflection is necessary. So it is established that a person lacking intellect and consciousness (whether a minor child or an adult insane) is not authorized to give amān to a disbeliever. Because for the party's acquaintance, intellect and consciousness are conditioned. Among the conditions of amān, one condition is that in the absence of puberty, the right of amān is impossible. Because in a minor child, the prohibition of fighting and the prohibition of address do not exist. Disputed case of amān by a minor: If the child is near puberty and has understanding of Islam, then according to Imam Muhammad, such a child has the right to give amān to a disbeliever. With the proof that eligibility for amān is based on eligibility for faith, and a minor child who has understanding of Islam falls into the category of people of faith. Initially, the minor child is authorized to give amān like an adult. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad in one opinion support Imam Muhammad's stance, and according to one narration, Imam Shafi‘i and Ahmad support Abu Hanifa's statement. While the majority of scholars (Hanafi companions) argue that a minor child is not among those eligible for amān in terms of knowledge of amān, because for the validity of amān, awareness of the secret conditions of Muslims and ability for deliberation and thought are necessary, which are not present in this minor child. Therefore, the Hanafis' opinion is that a minor child is not authorized to give amān considering the ruling of amān, provided that he is a minor who has understanding of Islam and is prohibited from fighting. So the amān of this minor child is like that of a 'abd majūr (a slave prohibited from fighting). Consensus case: If the child is permitted to fight, then due to having awareness of Muslims' secret condition (weakness and strength) and having understanding of Islam, according to all fuqahā' (especially Hanafi fuqahā'), unanimously the amān of such a child (permitted to fight) is valid. According to the author of Hidāyah or Qudūrī, the most correct opinion is this.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of amān (safe conduct) given by a minor. It begins by establishing the general principle that amān requires intellect and consciousness, thus excluding minors and the insane. Then it presents the specific case of a minor near puberty with understanding of Islam. Imam Muhammad permits it, arguing that amān eligibility is based on faith eligibility. Other Hanafis (jumhūr) reject it because a minor lacks the necessary awareness of Muslims' secret conditions. The passage notes that Imam Malik and Ahmad support Muhammad in one view, while Shāfi‘ī and Ahmad support Abu Hanifa in another. Finally, it reaches a consensus: if the minor is permitted to fight and has understanding, his amān is valid. The relied-upon position (as per Hidāyah/Qudūrī) is that such a minor's amān is valid.

Key Terms
امان (amān): Safe conduct granted to a disbeliever from enemy territory, ensuring protection of life and property.
صبی (ṣabī): A minor child who has not reached puberty, generally lacking legal capacity.
بلوغت (bulūgh): Puberty, the age of majority for legal responsibility.
قتال میں اجازت (qitāl meṉ ijāzat): Permission to fight, which in this context indicates that the minor is allowed to participate in military campaigns and thus becomes aware of Muslims' strategic conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is always invalid because minors lack capacity.
B) It is always valid if the minor understands Islam.
C) It is valid if the minor is permitted to fight and has understanding.
D) It is valid only if the minor has reached puberty.

Key Takeaway
A minor's amān is valid only if he has understanding of Islam and is permitted to fight; otherwise, the majority holds it invalid.
